The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Sent Personnel to Beijing to Participate in the Review of the Commercial Registration Law 131

Commissioners Chen and Luo Will Attend Tomorrow

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously stated that although the Civil Law Debt Article already has provisions for the responsibility of withdrawing from a partnership, there are no provisions for whether to add, change, or publish announcements after withdrawing from a partnership. Therefore, there have been disputes from time to time that have not been resolved for a long time. After a resolution was passed by the general meeting of members, it was submitted to the Legislative Yuan to formulate a commercial registration law so that the Civil Law Debt Management even has a layer of responsibility for currency, with room for adjustment and remedy. The Legislative Yuan replied and handed it over to the Commercial Law Committee to draft. It is now known that the drafting has been completed and will be held in Beijing on October 31st to review it. Yesterday, the association specially sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting to send representatives to attend and express their opinions. The association has appointed Chen Zheqing and Luo Qingten. The two commissioners will go to Beijing tomorrow to attend the meeting.

The Bank Law Research Association Held Its Second Meeting Yesterday 132

Banks Can Still Submit Opinions If They Have Any

According to the Central News Agency, the Bank Law Research Committee organized by the Bankers Association held its second meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 pm. All members attended, chaired by Xu Shenting. They continued to study the opinions put forward by the local Bankers Associations and various banks in this city, and combined them so that they could be submitted to the Ministry of Finance and the Legislative Yuan for adoption. In order to gather wisdom and benefit, the Bankers Association has further clarified the opinions of the local Bankers Associations and asked them to send their supplementary opinions to the Association within ten days so that they can be submitted for discussion. If the various banks in this city continue to have opinions, they can also submit them to the meeting within five days. The committee will conclude within two weeks and report the results of the research to the Executive Committee of the Xihang Public Association. It is reported that there are a total of 52 articles in the Bank Law. Article 5 stipulates that shareholders should bear double responsibility. All parties believe that it should be deleted. The old Bank Savings Law also had this provision, but it was deleted by the Bankers Association when it was discussed in the Legislative Yuan. Article 10 stipulates that banks shall not be shareholders of other companies, and it is believed that there is also a need for common methods in implementation. If shops and companies managed by banks due to mortgage loans are not allowed to continue operating, they will inevitably suffer losses. Therefore, it is hoped that there will be remedial measures in the implementation. There are many other opinions put forward by various parties, and it will take many meetings to draft a whole opinion.

Meeting Minutes of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce 133

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China held its 37th standing committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 pm. Those who attended were Li Kuian. Wen Lanting. Chen Riping. Lin Kanghou. Zhang Yuquan. (Lin Dai), etc., chaired by Chairman Lin Kanghou and recorded by Secretary Gu Huaibing. The resolutions of each case are as follows:

Appoint Representatives to Go to Beijing 134

1. Regarding the proposal to appoint representatives to the joint meeting of the Commercial Law and Civil Law Committees to review the Commercial Registration Law. Case: The association previously received letters and telegrams from various chambers of commerce stating that Article 681 of the Civil Law "Joint and several liability for partnership debts" is not average in terms of rights and obligations. The association forwarded it to the conference for amendments. The association repeatedly telegraphed the Legislative Yuan to request amendments. Later, the secretariat of the Legislative Yuan replied that the article does not need to be amended and that a commercial registration law will be formulated in the future to provide assistance. The association then telegraphed the Legislative Yuan again, requesting that personnel be allowed to attend the meeting when the commercial registration law is amended. Yesterday, the Commercial Law and Civil Law Committees of the Legislative Yuan sent a letter stating that the drafting of the commercial registration law has been completed and will be submitted for review at 9:00 am on the 31st of this month. Please appoint representatives to attend and express opinions. The association responded to the standing committee for discussion and decided how many representatives should be appointed and appointed. Resolved: Appoint Standing Committee Member Li Kuian to go to Beijing to attend the meeting.

Method of Exchanging Stamps 135

2. Regarding the proposal to have various chambers of commerce oppose the old stamp tax being registered in stages. Case: The association previously received a bulletin from the Ministry of Finance stating that new stamp tax tickets will be issued starting from November 1 this year, and the old stamp tax tickets will be invalidated at the same time. Subsequently, the association received letters and telegrams from various chambers of commerce requesting that the old stamps continue to be valid or that the old stamps be allowed to be used with the new stamps. The association repeatedly telegraphed the Central National Government and ministries to request. Later, the Ministry of Finance replied that considering the difficulties of business, if the old stamps have not been used up by November 1, a registration method will be determined to exchange them in stages. After the association notified, it received letters and telegrams from various chambers of commerce, either opposing the registration method, requesting that the old and new stamps continue to be used together, requesting an advance one-time exchange, or requesting the speedy determination of the registration method. How should it be handled? It is proposed to the Standing Committee for discussion and awaits a public decision. Resolved: Submit a request to the Ministry of Finance to determine the registration and exchange method as soon as possible.

Please Amend the Stamp Law 136

3. Regarding the proposal of various chambers of commerce to oppose the increased tax rates on invoices, leaflets, receipts, and ticket taxes under the Stamp Tax Law. Case: The association previously received letters and telegrams from various chambers of commerce stating that the temporary example of the Stamp Tax is harsh and incomplete, and requested that a stamp tax implementation law be formulated. The association repeatedly forwarded it to the Legislative Yuan, requesting it to be on file. Subsequently, on the 12th of this month, the 73rd meeting of the Legislative Yuan encountered the Stamp Tax Law, and although the starting point for stamping invoices, bills, and receipts was changed from one yuan to three yuan, it became a progressive method, from two cents to one yuan, which is 50 times more. Various chambers of commerce have requested to forward the amendments. The association has already telegraphed the Legislative Yuan twice, but many chambers of commerce continue to request it. Should it be telegraphed again? It is proposed to the Standing Committee for discussion and awaits a public decision. Resolved: Collect the opinions of various chambers of commerce and submit them to the Legislative Yuan to request amendments.

Promote the Organization of Provincial Chambers of Commerce 137

4. Regarding the proposal on how to promote the reorganization of chambers of commerce and the establishment of provincial federations of chambers of commerce. Case: The association previously failed to meet the statutory number of provincial federations of chambers of commerce and municipal chambers of commerce due to the reorganization, so the requests for reorganization were repeatedly ordered to maintain the status quo. Therefore, the association has been delayed and has not been reorganized to this day. The association has temporarily urged the reorganization of the various chambers of commerce and repeatedly telegraphed them, but most of them have not been completed. The association distributed a questionnaire in April of this year to investigate the reasons why the various chambers of commerce failed to reorganize. Subsequently, the various chambers of commerce filled out and returned the questionnaires to the association. The summary of the key points is that the reorganization of the chambers of commerce must be in accordance with the Chamber of Commerce Law, the Public Association Law, and the Regulations on the Organization of People's Organizations. The procedures are very complicated, and the merchants and people in the interior have less knowledge and cannot understand them, resulting in invisible stagnation. The association then formulated the organizational procedures for trade associations, chambers of commerce, and federations of chambers of commerce, printed them into a booklet, and distributed them to the national chambers of commerce for reference. Currently, there are 28 provinces in the country. Excluding Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Jehol for the time being, there are still 24 provinces and 5 special municipalities, totaling 29 units. According to Article 37 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, two-thirds should have 20 units to meet the statutory number. Currently, there are only three provincial federations of chambers of commerce in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Guangxi, and only four municipal chambers of commerce in Shanghai, Hankou, Beiping, and Qingdao have fully legal organizations. The rest are not sound and are far from the statutory number. How should we find ways to promote the reorganization of various chambers of commerce and the establishment of provincial federations of chambers of commerce? It is proposed to the Standing Committee for discussion and awaits a public decision. Resolved: Submit a request to the Ministry of Industry to urge the provinces that have not yet organized to reorganize quickly.

Letter to the Two Committees of the Legislative Yuan 138

The association drafted a letter to the Commercial Law Committee and the Civil Law Committee of the Legislative Yuan yesterday. The text was carried by Standing Committee Member Li Kuian. The original letter reads: In reply, on October 28 of this year, the letter from your association was received. The letter stated that the Commercial Registration Law had been resolved by the Yuan Council and handed over to the association to draft. The drafting has now been completed and will be reviewed at a joint meeting of the Commercial Law and Civil Law Committees in the Economic Committee Conference Room of the Yuan at 9:00 am on Wednesday, October 31. Accordingly, we hereby request your association to appoint representatives to attend, express their opinions, and hope to attend on time. When this was received, the 37th Standing Committee Meeting of the Association was held and resolved to appoint Standing Committee Member Li Kuian as the representative to review the Commercial Registration Law. We hereby reply to your association and hope that you will investigate and take care of the official affairs.

The Process of Issuing Corporate Bonds by the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company 140

According to the Central News Agency, the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company suffered huge losses during the January 28th Incident. Now, the local authorities in this city are actively seeking the revival of the war zone and the prosperity of the city center, and have specially approved the company to issue corporate bonds. The negotiation process and the company bond charter are recorded as follows:

Negotiation Process 141

The Zhabei Water and Electricity Company suffered heavy losses in both water and electricity during the January 28th Incident. After the war, the market was sluggish, and the losses suffered in business were also not praised. After repeated consultations among shareholders, they jointly sought revival and submitted a request to the municipal authorities to allow the issuance of company bonds in order to repay old debts and expand equipment. The municipal authorities believe that the war zone is in urgent need of revival, and the city center is in urgent need of prosperity. Repaying is also a real situation. The request was transferred to the National Construction Committee, which approved the company to issue 6 million yuan of company bonds. The company contacted the Bank of Communications, the Four Lines Savings Society, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Jin Cheng Bank, and the Chinese Medicine Encouragement Bank in this city to manage the bonds and keep the collateral for the bonds. The banks formed a bond management committee, the company manages, and the Four Lines Savings Society is designated to be responsible for safekeeping and collection and payment.

Issuance Method 142

The first phase of these bonds will raise 4.5 million yuan. The bonds are divided into two types: 10,000 yuan and 1,000 yuan. They are unregistered, but if the bondholder requests, they can be changed to registered. The bonds are issued at 98% of the par value, that is, 98 yuan will be actually received for every 100 yuan. The interest rate is 8% per annum, calculated from the date of issuance. Interest is paid every half year, and one-sixteenth of the principal is repaid every half year by lottery. All will be paid off after eight years. These bonds are limited to those of Chinese nationality in traditional Chinese medicine, and it is scheduled to be raised from 10:00 am to 12:00 pm tomorrow at the five banks managed by the Bank of Communications.

Issuance Charter 143

Article 1: Zhabei Water and Electricity Co., Ltd. (hereinafter referred to as the "Company") will issue company bonds in order to repay old debts and expand equipment, as resolved at the 8th shareholders' meeting on February 26, 1933. Article 2: According to the provisions of the Company Law and the Electrical Business Regulations, and according to the ratio of the paid-up share capital of 6 million yuan and the fixed assets of 13,669,000 yuan at the end of 1933 (omitting those below 1,000 yuan), the total amount of company bonds is stipulated to be 6 million yuan, which will be raised in phases according to the company's needs. Article 3: The company will raise 4.5 million yuan of bonds in the first phase, which is scheduled to be raised by October 31, 1934. The date for raising the second phase of bonds will be announced at that time. Article 4: The holder of this bond is invalid if he is of the nationality of the Republic of China. Article 5: The company bonds are secured by all of the fixed assets listed in the company's balance sheet and property catalog at the end of 1933, with a total value of 13,669,000 yuan (omitting those below 1,000 yuan) as the joint guarantee for the bonds, and the first mortgage and pledge rights are set up. The catalog and deeds are transferred to the bank managing the bonds for safekeeping. If the company fails to pay the principal and interest of the bonds for two periods, the bank managing the bonds may dispose of all or part of the collateral upon the request of the bondholders' representatives with more than half of the claim amount. Article 6: The company entrusts the Bank of Communications, the Four Lines Savings Society, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Jin Cheng Bank, and the Chinese Medicine Encouragement Bank (hereinafter referred to as the "Bank") to manage and issue the bonds and keep the collateral for the bonds. The contract between the company and the bank for management shall be determined separately. Article 7: The Bank represents the interests of the bondholders and has the right to examine the company's financial, business, and engineering conditions, consult the relevant documents and receipts, and provide opinions to the company's board of directors. The Bank shall appoint an accountant to reside in the company to audit the various accounts. Article 8: The interest rate on the bonds is 8% per annum, calculated from the date of issuance, and interest is paid every half year. Article 9: The bonds are issued at 98% of the par value, that is, 98 yuan will be actually received for every 100 yuan. Article 10: The bonds have a term of eight years, calculated from the date of issuance, and one-sixteenth of the number of bonds issued will be redeemed every half year by lottery, until the 16th period of eight years is satisfied, and all will be paid off. Article 11: The bonds are divided into two types: 10,000 yuan and 1,000 yuan. They are generally unregistered, but they can be changed to registered at the request of the bondholder. When registered bonds are transferred, they must go through transfer procedures and remain registered bonds. Unregistered bonds rely solely on the bonds to collect principal and interest. If they are lost, they will not be replaced. Article 12: The company shall allocate the principal and interest due for each bond from the income and deposit it with the bank first for payment when due. Article 13: After the bond is drawn, the bondholder shall present the original bond, together with the attached unmatured coupons, to the bank for payment. If the attached coupons are missing, the amount shall be deducted from the principal. Article 14: The drawn bonds and matured coupons shall be collected from the bank within 24 months. If they are not collected after the deadline, they shall be cancelled immediately. Article 15: Matters not covered in these regulations shall be governed by the provisions of the Company Law and other relevant laws and regulations. Article 16: These regulations shall be submitted by the Shanghai Public Utilities Bureau to the Shanghai Municipal Government for review and transferred to the National Construction Committee and the Ministry of Industry for review and approval.

Inauguration of the Fourth Freight Training Class 145

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations inaugurated the fourth freight training class. The director addressed the audience, stating that the administration had organized three sessions in Shanghai to host representatives from various companies, factories, and stores, explaining railway freight procedures and providing tours of railway freight operations. Due to the enthusiastic participation of these businesses, a fourth session was planned. However, this will be the last session held in Shanghai, as future sessions will be conducted in Nanjing and Hangzhou to ensure balanced coverage. The director emphasized that the purpose of the freight training classes has been explained at the opening of each of the previous three sessions. While the specific content varied, the ultimate goal remained the same. At the inauguration of the fourth session, he summarized the previous points and presented two key objectives: Firstly, from the perspective of the entire production industry, the administration's involvement in these freight matters encompasses three aspects. From the railway's standpoint, both production and sales represent shippers. Legal regulations govern the relationship between railways and freight merchants, but merchants often find them complex and difficult to understand. In the past, the railway may not have sufficiently ensured that merchants fully understood these regulations. Therefore, the administration, to demonstrate its sincerity in cooperation, specifically invites merchants to learn about the freight handling procedures and calculation methods used by the railway, revealing all details and encouraging them to visit stations and freight yards for on-site observation to eliminate misunderstandings and facilitate collaboration. This is the fundamental purpose of the administration's freight training classes, to promote national economic development based on fairness and mutual benefit. Secondly, every enterprise should have an organizational structure to thrive. This structure can be divided into three aspects: the organization of the enterprise itself, such as the internal organization of a company or factory, or industry associations. Another is the organization of related enterprises, such as the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. Considering the three aspects of production, transportation, and sales, each individual sector already has a well-established organization. Vertically, production and sales also have substantial organization, but there is no adequate organization linking production, transportation, and sales. Therefore, the administration promotes cooperation among these three sectors and proposes establishing a joint organization. For example, in stations with particularly developed freight operations, the administration intends to convene a committee comprising shippers from both the production and sales sides, along with railway representatives, to jointly inspect freight operations regularly. This proposal has already been approved by the Ministry of Railways. In addition, the administration envisions a club-like organization to foster communication and exchange ideas among the three sectors. After the completion of this final freight training session in Shanghai, the administration plans to convene all the companies, factories, and stores that have participated in previous sessions to discuss implementation. This is the administration's major hope for the freight training classes, and it seeks the continued support and guidance of everyone involved.

Central Committee Member Wang Qi Discusses Art Movement 146

According to the Central News Agency, Central Committee Member Wang Qi arrived in Shanghai to prepare for his personal calligraphy and painting exhibition. Yesterday, a reporter visited his residence and inquired about his views on the art movement. Wang Qi stated that he believes the art industry is essential for the survival of the nation and state. Human evolution relies on shared intellectual capacity to create culture and improve society, meeting the needs of both the present and future generations. Westerners refer to humans as rational animals, distinguished from other creatures by their noble character, refined lifestyle, and ability to socialize and share this lifestyle. This lifestyle should have both internal (spiritual) and external (material) aspects, which are interdependent and mutually supportive. Overemphasis on one aspect leads to imbalance and deficiency, preventing the formation of a fulfilling life. In recent times, human desires have run rampant, with an extreme tendency towards material life, resulting in corruption and deterioration. During this period of national crisis, people should uplift their spirits, cultivate noble characters, and engage in social reform. Satisfying basic needs like food, clothing, shelter, and transportation is essential, but moral education is even more critical. Wang Qi has no personal hobbies and spends his free time studying calligraphy and painting, albeit with limited achievements. He has joined many art and literary organizations over the years. Last year, he and other art professionals in Beijing initiated the Chinese Art Association, including Zhang Ji, Yu Youren, Chen Shuren, Jing Tinggu, Zhang Dao藩, Yu Jingtang, Hong Ludong, Liang Dingming, Tang Wenting, and professors from National Central University like Li Yishi, Chen Zhifo, Pan Yuliang, and Zhang Shuqi, as well as professors from Nanjing Art School like Gao Xishun and Zhang Yiran. Chen Guofu and Chen Lifu strongly supported the initiative. Recently, Xu Beihong returned from Europe and joined the association. The association's purpose is to unite the national art community in promoting art and cultural movements, revitalizing Chinese art and literature while advocating new ideas and building new enterprises, without any distinction between the old and the new. A commemorative exhibition was held in Beijing a month ago, showcasing a wide range of works, including paintings, calligraphy, sculptures, and industrial arts. Members from various fields contributed exhibits, including Wang Yachen, Zhang Yuguang, Zhu Xianyun, Zhu Qizhan, and Cheng Zhenxia from Shanghai, many of whom attended the event. The association originally planned to establish branches in Shanghai, Beijing, and Hangzhou, which are currently underway. Wang Qi also intends to facilitate some connections during this trip.

Lake Society Letter to County Magistrates in the Lake Region 147

Encouraging Spring Planting: Supplementing Agricultural Production

The Lake Society of this city, recognizing the severe drought and resulting crop failure in the Lake region, has sent letters to the six county magistrates in the region, urging them to encourage spring planting to remedy the situation. The letter states: "Regarding the fact that our six counties in the Lake region have suffered from drought for months since the summer, with scorching sun and parched land, despite all efforts to mitigate the effects, the rivers and canals have dried up, dashing all hopes. Farmers, already struggling with years of poor harvests, have no surplus grain, and starvation is widespread. Our society, deeply concerned about this plight, has joined forces with fellow natives in Shanghai to establish the Lake Region Disaster Relief Committee, seeking aid to provide some relief. However, in this time of economic decline and widespread poverty, the funds raised are likely limited and may not last until next spring. With the Double Ninth Festival passed and Minor Spring approaching, recent rainfall has slightly moistened the land, making it not too late to sow spring crops. Although it may be a small effort, it can still supplement agricultural production. No land should be left uncultivated, as the people's livelihood depends on hard work. We cannot afford to let disaster halt daily activities and simply wait for death. Therefore, we specifically request that Your Excellency, the County Magistrate, promptly issue proclamations, explaining the benefits of spring planting to prevent idleness and lead to wrongdoings. Please also instruct the district chiefs to widely promote and supervise the planting efforts. We eagerly await your response."

Disaster Reports from Various Regions: Begging for Relief and Urgent Appeals - Haining 148

This year's drought is the worst among the counties in the Jiangnan region, affecting over 300,000 people in the entire county. Recently, local charitable organizations such as the Jisheng Society, the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, the Bodhi Dharma Society, and the Red Swastika Society have jointly provided emergency relief. After strict verification by the county government, the number of people in need of assistance still exceeds 140,000. However, due to the vast area affected, the total amount of emergency relief funds is only around 70,000 to 80,000 yuan, which is only enough to provide food for a few days. Therefore, for a widespread relief effort, providing work in exchange for wages is essential. Mr. Feng Liutang, a standing committee member of the Haining County Drought Relief Association, proposed repairing the Sixty Black Pond River and organizing work projects along the coast. A meeting was convened at the Gongdelin Office in Shanghai to discuss this proposal. The participants unanimously agreed that the Sixty Li Pond River in Haining, which connects to the Shangtang River in the west, encircles the county seat, and ends at Huangwan in the east, is located in the southern part of the county and is at a high elevation. In the past, frequent storm surges caused breaches in the riverbanks, leading to sediment deposition and eventual blockage. As a result, irrigation of farmland on both banks suffered, and sixty li of transportation was cut off. Previous proposals to repair the river were never implemented. The river is crucial for the farmland and water resources in the southern part of the county, and the average annual grain production in the area along the river is less than half of what it used to be due to the blockage and lack of dredging. Therefore, the participants decided that the river repair project is essential for providing work relief. However, due to the large scale and high cost of the project, it cannot be undertaken without substantial funding from the government through public bonds. It has been reported that the association has sent a letter to the county government, requesting a prompt estimate of the project costs and submitting it to the provincial government, urging them to consider the severity of the disaster in Haining County, which is unparalleled compared to other counties, and approve the allocation of funds for the work relief project as a priority.

Yuqian 149

Yuqian County, located on the border of western Zhejiang under the jurisdiction of Hangzhou, encompasses the West Tianmu Mountain within its boundaries. The county is predominantly mountainous with limited farmland, making it naturally barren. In years of good harvests, the yield barely covers the population's needs. Since the beginning of summer this year, the county has experienced continuous drought for nearly three months. The soil has cracked, and the crops have withered. After autumn, heavy rain fell, reviving the withered crops. However, due to the sudden cold weather, the revived seedlings withered again, resulting in a complete crop failure. According to investigations by the Central Relief Commission, the degree of damage far exceeds ninety percent, with disaster victims accounting for over seventy percent of the county's population. Those without rice to cook use paper mulberry leaves, bitter vegetables, and mountain grains to fill their stomachs. The suffering is unbearable, and reports of suicides due to hardship are frequent. Mr. Shen Naigeng, the county magistrate, along with local representatives, arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday and has been visiting leaders of various relief organizations, reporting on the disaster situation and requesting immediate assistance to alleviate the suffering of the disaster victims.

Langxi 150

An Appeal to Kindhearted Benefactors at Home and Abroad from the Shen Bao Newspaper: In the reigns of Yao and Tang, there were floods and droughts, yet the people did not suffer from cold or hunger. During the famines and epidemics in the states of Su and Zhao, the descendants did not worry about displacement. Alas, our Langxi region is afflicted by drought, with calamities descending from the heavens. For three months, there has been no rain, causing sorrow for the hundred thousand people. Thirty-eight thousand acres of fertile land have seen their crops wither. Ninety-six villages are suffering, with people displaying a wretched appearance. Some are wandering, some are displaced, some are hungry, and some are thirsty, resembling emaciated birds, filling the air with laments. Ditches, canals, and rivers have all cracked. Rural areas are declining, and people cannot even obtain a single bowl of gruel. Bandits are rampant, and the crisis is further compounded by widespread robberies of grain. There are reports of selling wives and children, causing painful separations that resemble lingering deaths. The plight of refugees depicted by Zheng Xia is now evident in Langxi. We issue passionate appeals, seeking assistance from those in authority. We had hoped for a bountiful autumn harvest, but the crops have withered. We had expected relief from the spring famine, but now winter is approaching, which is even more difficult to endure. An investigation of the population in each district reveals a shortage of over three hundred thousand dan of grain. Statistics show that less than twenty percent of the land in the entire county has yielded a small harvest, while the rest is barren. Now, the eastern crops have failed, with withered branches and leaves. It is to be feared that the western crops will also be disappointing. How can we collect salt taxes and pay for goods? There is no way to provide relief from the famine. We earnestly appeal to you to have compassion for the disaster victims, provide abundant provisions, and generously distribute relief funds. It is also requested that both work relief and winter relief be provided concurrently, and that both grain relief and financial aid be offered equally. It is said that providing shade with the leaves of a large tree is akin to creating a dense canopy, and reducing a spoonful of water from the Yangtze River is akin to creating a healing balm. Giving the disaster victims a chance to live is like granting them a new life. We earnestly request you to provide more assistance, which will save more lives. The Disaster Relief Committee, Finance Committee, Chamber of Commerce, Farmers' Association, Education Association, and Civil Food Relief Committee respectfully bow three times in gratitude.

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to the Public Works Department Suggesting Improvements to Traffic Issues 151

Maintaining Streetcars and Preventing Parallel Operation with Buses

Ensuring Citizen Safety and Handling Vehicle Accidents According to Law

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association sent a letter to the Director-General of the Public Works Department yesterday, stating: "We are writing to you regarding the frequent traffic accidents that have occurred within the First Special District in recent years, jeopardizing the safety of citizens. For ordinary vehicles, strict inspections and penalties ensure that drivers are cautious beforehand and that compensation is provided afterward, maintaining a balance. However, public buses, due to the involvement of multiple parties, face leniency in inspections and often avoid responsibility for accidents. As a result, drivers become reckless and negligent, further compromising citizen safety. We have seen reports that your Traffic Committee has been discussing traffic issues in the district. While various proposals have been made, we believe that further detailed and thorough consideration is necessary. As a representative of taxpayers, our association has gathered public opinion and reached the following conclusions: 1. All efforts should consider local conditions and adapt to local needs, rather than simply following foreign examples. 2. Streetcars should be maintained, and the Public Works Department should take over their operation when the concession expires. 3. Public buses should not operate on the same routes as streetcars, and the buses should be smaller, similar to those used in the Second District. Double-decker buses should not be allowed to operate on busy roads. 4. The safety of citizens should be fully guaranteed. All vehicles, whether public or private, should be subject to legal proceedings in case of accidents, without exception. If found guilty, the vehicle owner should bear civil liability, and the Public Works Department should provide assistance, such as revoking licenses. We hope that you will consider these suggestions and take appropriate action."

Rickshaw Owners Petition the Public Works Department to Protest the Forced Replacement of Rickshaws 153

Result: Seized Rickshaw Licenses Returned, Deadline Set for Replacement

Rickshaw Owners Claim It's Difficult to Comply, Will Continue to Fight

Rickshaw owners affected by the Public Works Department's Fairness Road Rickshaw Inspection Office's forced replacement of rickshaw licenses and new rickshaws, led by Te Zheng Biao, Yan Zheng Bao, Liang Yu Hua, Le He Lin, Zhu Xue Cheng, Tang Guang Liang, Ren Lu Qi, Jin Chun Lin, Xue Zhang Pei Hua, Chu Lian Gui, Zhao Rong Fu, Xue Zheng Ji, and over sixty others, went to the Rickshaw Committee at 10:00 AM yesterday to petition. They elected Jin Chun Lin, Xue Zheng Ji, and Zhao Rong Fu as representatives to meet with Committee Chairman Massey and members Zhu Mao Cheng and Wang Zhi Ren. They requested the issuance of licenses and expressed their inability to accept the new rickshaws. The Rickshaw Committee ordered the head of the Inspection Office to attend for questioning regarding the unauthorized seizure of licenses and forced removal of seals, deeming it inappropriate. According to reporters from Xin Sheng News, licenses have been forcibly removed from six rickshaw groups, and over eighty rickshaws have been ordered to be replaced with new ones within one month. However, based on the eighth resolution of the Rickshaw Owners Committee's meeting on August 6, the new public rickshaw design should be based on the practical suggestions of rickshaw pullers and other relevant parties and can only be implemented after all parties agree. This was approved by the Public Works Department Board of Directors on August 7. The forced replacement without the consent of all parties has caused great dissatisfaction among the rickshaw owners. At 2:00 PM, the six seized licenses were returned. The owners were given one month to replace all rickshaws with new ones to standardize them. However, the rickshaw owners claim that replacing all rickshaws with the new design within one month is impossible and that the new design is impractical. They have vowed to continue their fight.

Shanghai County Third Agricultural Exhibition Preparatory Meeting 157

The first preparatory meeting for the Shanghai County Third Agricultural Exhibition was held on October 26 at 10:00 AM at the Yutang Muai Church. Pudong Water Plant to Begin Operation in April Next Year 159

Municipal Industrial Development Society Plans to Submit Proposal

To the Municipal Government for Approval and Construction

The Shanghai Municipal Industrial Development Trust Society, after receiving instructions from the Municipal Government to actively prepare for the Pudong Water Plant, immediately began designing the project. The society recognized the vast area of Pudong and its unlimited potential for future development. Therefore, the water plant was planned based on two principles: 1. To ensure widespread water supply to the entire region; 2. To keep water prices as low as possible. Based on these principles, the water plant's maximum daily water supply capacity must be 13,636.5 cubic meters (approximately 3 million gallons) to meet the needs. The plant site must occupy at least 15 mu (approximately 2.5 acres). Therefore, the initial design was carefully considered to avoid future difficulties in expansion due to land constraints. The inability of the old Zhabei Water Plant to expand, leading to the construction of a new plant, serves as a cautionary tale. The society had to find a way to expedite the water plant's operation. After careful research, it came up with two options: a formal water plant and a temporary water plant. The formal water plant would be larger in scale and take approximately one year to complete. The temporary water plant would be built on public land in Pudong, consisting of a water storage pool. It would adopt a water purchase and transfer method, using water tankers to purchase clean water from the water plant, taking advantage of the night-time ferry downtime to transport the water. Electric centrifugal pumps would then pump the water into the storage pool, where it would be further disinfected. This method is expected to deliver water by April next year at the latest. The society has submitted this plan to the Municipal Government for review and approval.

Dismissal of Police Appeal in the Xue Mai-Luo Robbery Case 160

Zhang Zuming and Four Others Acquitted

The case involving the robbery of 12,000 yuan from the accounting firm of Xue Mai-Luo, in which the suspects Zhang Zuming, Zhuang Jimeng, Wang Lianyou, and Tang Qingyue were implicated and arrested by the French police, has concluded its trial at the Second Special District Local Court. The court acquitted all four defendants. Dissatisfied with the verdict, the French Police Department appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. After a thorough investigation by the High Court, the presiding judge, accompanied by the prosecutor, visited the scene of the crime. Following deliberations by the collegiate panel, a date was set for the pronouncement of the verdict, as reported extensively in the newspapers. Yesterday afternoon, on the day of the verdict, the appellants Zhang Zuming, Zhuang Jimeng, Wang Lianyou, and Tang Qingyue, along with the plaintiff, Zhou Jinggeng, and their respective defense attorneys Lin Yingqing, E Sen, Li Guozhen, and Yan Yinwu, arrived at the court to await the decision. The Police Department was represented by attorney Yuan Jiahuang. At 2:30 PM, Judge Guo Dezhang (presiding over the case as acting presiding judge in place of Judge Sun Honglin, who was on leave visiting relatives in his hometown of Jing) and Judges Zhang Chaozuo and Li Shouyi, together with Prosecutor Zhang Zongru, convened a special session of the Third Criminal Court. The four appellants, Zhang, Zhuang, Wang, and Tang, were brought before the court, and after a brief questioning, the verdict was read aloud, dismissing the appeal. Subsequently, the plaintiff, Zhou Jinggeng, was brought before the court, and the verdict dismissing the accompanying civil appeal was announced. After the verdicts were read, the court briefly explained their meaning and informed the four appellants that they would remain on their original bail during the period for appealing to the Third Instance Court.

Jiang-Zhejiang Water Police Brigade Cracks Down on Fishermen's Provocations 165

The Jiang-Zhejiang Water Police Brigade has issued a public notice stating that, according to reports from fishery associations, fishermen's trade associations, and the Renhe, Linghe, and Jinghe Public Offices, every fishing season, fishermen from various regions gather to fish in the Jiang-Zhejiang waters. However, some individuals, whose character is questionable, resort to barbaric acts such as seizing nets, dragging people, and extorting money upon encountering other boats. Some even sail into the ocean without their own fishing gear, intentionally provoking others under the cover of darkness, seizing their nets for their own gain. This not only harms others and benefits themselves, obstructing fishing, but is also tantamount to robbery under the guise of fishing. If not suppressed, the future of fishing is unimaginable. Therefore, a joint petition was submitted, urgently requesting the issuance of an order to stop these actions and requesting that coastal military and police agencies pay close attention to eliminate these miscreants and maintain the fishing industry. In response, the Water Police Brigade has determined that the actions of fishermen who use pretexts to provoke others and drag people are in violation of the law. If such actions are not strictly suppressed, the fishing industry cannot be maintained and public safety cannot be ensured. Based on the aforementioned reports, the Brigade, in addition to ordering its ships to pay attention to preventing such incidents, hereby issues a public notice to all fishermen, informing them that if any incidents of obstructing the fishing industry occur in the future, they will be arrested and prosecuted without leniency. Everyone must strictly comply. This notice is hereby issued.

Stealing a Gun to Plot Murder 167

Arrested Before the Deed Could Be Done

Debate Concluded, Date Set for Pronouncement

Wang Taoji, a 23-year-old rickshaw puller from Tongzhou, often parked his rickshaw at the entrance of Meilan Lane on Belle Road in the French Concession. He became acquainted with Gu Pei, the watchman of the lane, and often stayed in the watchman's small wooden booth. Wang had a long-standing grudge against Jiang Shijin, a 28-year-old fellow townsman who lived at No. 5, Lane 103, Xinqiao Road in the Chinese area and had previously worked as a detective in the Public Security Bureau. Wang had repeatedly thought of ways to harm Jiang, but lacked the means to do so. One day, Wang saw that the watchman was wearing a handgun issued by the police station. On the evening of September 22nd, while Gu Pei was on duty, Wang stole the handgun and six bullets that were hanging in the small wooden booth. He hid them on his person and fled. Gu discovered the theft and reported it to the French Police, requesting an arrest. After stealing the handgun, Wang invited Jiang Shibiao to meet him in the wilderness of Bazibiao, Zhabei. He intended to shoot Jiang, but Jiang was unaware of Wang's sinister intentions. He invited his fellow townsman, Dai Xiaojin, a 23-year-old rickshaw puller who lived at No. 15, Deren Lane, Guohuo Road in the southern city, to accompany him to Bazibiao, Zhabei. While they were talking, a police detective from the Public Security Bureau arrived on patrol and found Wang and the others suspicious. They searched them and found the handgun and bullets on Wang's person. Wang, Jiang, and Dai were taken to the police station and transferred to the Shanghai Local Court for interrogation. After learning of the incident, the French Police reported it to the Second Special District Court and requested that detectives be dispatched to the Local Court to transfer Wang, Dai, and Jiang, along with the handgun, to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and detention. The handgun and bullets were returned to Gu Pei. Yesterday morning, Judge Tai Yangping interrogated them in the First Criminal Court. The police attorney, Fei Xizhen, explained the police investigation and charged Wang Taoji with attempted murder and theft under Article 284 of the Criminal Code. Dai Xiaojin and Jiang Shibiao were charged with suspicion of theft. Wang Taoji confessed to stealing the handgun and intending to kill Jiang. Dai and Jiang both testified that they were unaware of Wang Taoji's theft of the handgun. After a lengthy investigation, the court declared the debate closed and set the pronouncement for the 30th. The defendants were returned to custody.

Lewd Monk's Bestial Behavior 168

A Friend's Daughter Grossly Violated

The Law Should Impose Severe Sanctions

The lewd monk Yang Tang, originally from Gaoyou, is currently 38 years old. He was formerly a monk at the Baiyun Temple, but because he had not cleansed his six senses and failed to abide by the monastic rules, he was expelled by the abbot. He now resides upstairs in the waiting room at No. 224, North Fujian Road, and thus became acquainted with Miao Yaoting, a tenant from Taizhou who lives in the porter's lodge of the house. Recently, the monk suddenly moved to No. 157 nearby. At around 3:00 PM on the 20th of this month, Hui Tang visited Miao Yaoting for a chat. Upon entering Miao's room, he found that Miao and his wife, Gu, had gone out and had not yet returned. Only their ten-year-old daughter, A Bao, was left in the room to watch the door. Hui Tang looked around and, seeing no one, was overcome with lust. He suddenly became extremely bold, closed the door, took out fifteen copper coins from his pocket as bait, gave them to A Bao, and embraced her. First, he played with the girl's lower body with his fingers. Then, driven by sexual desire, he forcibly raped her. A Bao was an ignorant child and, of course, had no strength to resist. A Bao did not dare to say anything. But Hui Tang was a lewd monk who, because he did not abide by the monastic rules, was fond of engaging in licentious activities, and thus contracted a venereal disease. After committing adultery with the girl once, the symptoms of leucorrhea were transmitted to her. For several days, the girl not only walked unsteadily, but her underwear was also covered in white spots and bloody stains. Her mother became suspicious and questioned her severely. Only then did she tell the truth about being raped by the monk. Upon hearing this, Miao and his wife were enraged and knew that the so-called monk must be Hui Tang. At 8:45 PM the night before last, they went to Hui Tang's residence to confront him. In his desperation, he swallowed a small amount of opium, hoping to commit suicide, and fled into the street. Miao then called Chinese Constable No. 2647, who arrived and took Hui Tang to the Huisih Police Station. The young girl, Miao A Bao, was sent to Guangren Hospital, where it was confirmed that her hymen had been ruptured and that she had contracted leucorrhea and would need to be hospitalized for treatment. A medical certificate was issued and brought back to the police station by the detectives. Under questioning, Hui Tang initially admitted to playing with his fingers but denied rape. However, a medical certificate from the Tongsheng Pharmacy found on his person revealed that he had indeed suffered from leucorrhea and had gone to the pharmacy to seek treatment for five dollars, which had not yet been cured. Hui Tang was sent to Tongren and Patrol Police Hospitals for examinations, which confirmed that he had leucorrhea. Both hospitals issued certificates as evidence. Therefore, yesterday morning, the police first brought Hui Tang to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District and charged him with rape under Article 240, Paragraph 2, of the Criminal Code. The police attorney, Zhang Tianyin, explained the above situation and requested an adjournment because the victim, Miao A Bao, was still in the hospital and could not be present in court today. Judge Wu ruled that, because the case involved public morals, spectators were prohibited from attending. As a result, the case was adjourned for seven days for further hearing. The defendant, Hui Tang, was ordered to undergo a forensic examination before being taken back to the police station for detention.

No Grudges, Yet This Cruel Act

Request for Adjournment to Conduct Investigation

Ji Xiangyun, a native of Wuxi and the owner of the Fengyi Printing House located at No. 1299, Siwen Lane, Datong Road, was tricked into coming out at 8:05 AM on the 27th of this month. The detectives investigated the claim and discovered that it was entirely false, as Guo was not married. After repeated questioning, Guo confessed that the idea came from Li Aju, who was at large. Li had a long-standing feud with Ji and, for revenge, recruited Zhang Xinglong and Guo. They first discussed the plan at the Tianchan Tea House on Xizang Road, deciding to disfigure Ji's face with nitric acid. At around 8:00 AM on the morning of the incident, Li Aju waited outside Ji's door with a glass of nitric acid. When Ji arrived, Guo and Li poured the nitric acid on his face, disfiguring him. Guo was then arrested. Upon hearing this confession, the police questioned Ji Xiangyun. Ji stated that he did not know Li Aju and had no grudges against her. Therefore, he believed there was more to the case and requested an adjournment to apprehend the accomplices. Ji Xiangyun also filed a complaint, stating that the defendant had come to his home a few days earlier, pretending to be interested in renting a room. Although they usually had a rental sign posted, he did not pay attention at the time. Thinking back, he realized that the man was probably using the pretext of renting to observe his face. He did not recognize Li Aju and believed that there was more to the case. He knew that a former accountant in his shop, a Mr. Li, had committed theft and was prosecuted by him. Mr. Li was sentenced to imprisonment but was appealing the verdict, and the case was scheduled to be heard that afternoon. Therefore, the defendant may have been instigated by Mr. Li. He requested that the police not only apprehend the accomplices but also reserve the right to seek compensation for all damages. When questioned, the defendant, Han Yongzhang, admitted to pouring nitric acid. Judge Wu reviewed the confession and ordered Guo to be detained for further hearing on November 2nd.

Major Fire in Zhabei's Huazi Creek 171

Dozens of Shanties Destroyed

Two Children Burned to Death

A major fire broke out in Huazi Creek, which is under the jurisdiction of the Tanziwan Police Station in Zhabei, yesterday morning. Dozens of shanties were destroyed, and a mother and her son, Zhang Wu and her son, perished in the fire. The details are as follows:

Observation of the Fire Site 172

The fire site was located at the western end of Zhongxing Road, south of the Dayangqiao Railway Bridge, at the eastern end of Panjiawan. Although the area was already urbanized, many shanties were interspersed with tiled bungalows, and some did not have house numbers. The fire site faced the Suzhou Creek and was backed by the Huazi Creek. Across the creek on both sides were also clusters of shanties and a small number of tiled bungalows. Approximately sixty to seventy shanties were destroyed, covering an area of about seven to eight acres.

Circumstances of the Fire 173

At around 4:00 AM yesterday morning, the poor residents of the area were still asleep. A fire suddenly broke out in the shanty of Yang Junxiang (38 years old, a plasterer from Funing) along the creek in the northeast. Constable Li Maozhen, stationed at Post No. 52 nearby, saw the fire, called the Fire Department to come and extinguish it, and reported it to the Tanziwan Police Station. Patrol Officer Li Qingjie led the patrol police to maintain order. Unfortunately, the area was not equipped with fire hydrants, and there was no way to draw water at the time. Moreover, the northeast wind was very strong, and the flames spread to the southwest. Water was drawn from Dayangqiao and transported over the railway for firefighting. The fire was finally extinguished at around 6:00 AM.

Discovery of Corpses 174

When the fire broke out, Yang Junxiang's shanty had two rooms. He lived in one, and the other was rented to Zhang Deyou from Qingjiang. Zhang had returned to his hometown to sell old goods, leaving only his wife, Wu (40 years old), and son, An Chenzi (13 years old), at home. Unfortunately, Wu and her son were unable to escape and perished in the fire. At the time, thousands of poor people were helping the elderly and children, grabbing their belongings, and fleeing for their lives, causing great disorder. No one knew that Wu and her son had perished in the fire. At around 8:00 AM, after a search, two corpses were discovered. Wu was found lying face down in the ashes, and An Chenzi was lying face up on a board. His limbs had fallen off, and his entire body was charred beyond recognition. The sight was extremely tragic. According to neighbors, Wu was a devout Buddhist who burned incense, lit candles, and chanted scriptures daily. Therefore, everyone called her "Grandma Dao."

Reporting for Autopsy 175

After the incident, Patrol Officer Li of the Tanziwan Police Station sent Yang Junxiang, the source of the fire, to the Xin Zha Public Security Bureau for questioning. Meanwhile, he ordered Chen Quansheng, the local head of the twelfth district, to report to the Shanghai Local Court for an autopsy. At around 5:00 PM, Inspector Zhang Zixuan arrived at the scene and confirmed that the deceased, Zhang Wu and Zhang Anchen, mother and son, had died from being burned alive. The local head was instructed to make arrangements for their burial. According to the subsequent investigation, the fire was believed to have been caused by incense and candles that were lit in the rented room of Yang Junxiang and had not been completely extinguished when everyone went to bed. The candles may have fallen onto the straw, causing the fire. The fire site has been cleared, and no other corpses were found until late at night.

The judge then rigorously questioned each defendant about their actions during the commission of the crimes and their behavior before and after the crimes. Money Gone, Love Lost, Treated Like Strangers: Tragedy Brews in a Temple Alley 177

A Razor in Hand, Resolved to Perish Together

Meeting on a Narrow Path, Cutting His Lover and Then Himself

Yan A'tu from Suzhou, thirty years old, used to make a small living in his hometown. Having accumulated some savings, in April of this year, Yan unexpectedly encountered Wu Dai'shi, a woman from the same village, thirty-two years old. They fell in love at first sight, forming an inextricable bond. However, because there were many eyes and ears in Suzhou, they could not do as they pleased. After several discussions, they resolutely took a train to Shanghai on April 26th, rented a house together, and lived as husband and wife. For several months, they were quite affectionate. However, the cost of living in Shanghai was high, and their savings were limited, making it unsustainable for them to simply sit and eat. In the past two months, they gradually felt the strain. Initially, Yan still caught crickets to earn a small profit, but now, as the weather grew colder, it was no longer the season for crickets, and he could not maintain their livelihood. The woman, on the other hand, was of a fickle nature. Seeing that Yan's money was running out and knowing that it would be difficult to grow old together, she broke away from Yan a month ago and became involved with another man, living with him at No. 30, Miaolong Lane, Jing'an Temple Road. After that, they occasionally met on the road, but the woman treated him like a stranger. Until recently, about a week ago, Yan encountered the woman again near the small vegetable market on Hardoon Road. Yan, facing financial difficulties and being unfamiliar with the people and places of Shanghai, had no one to turn to for help. Overwhelmed by hunger, he asked the woman for assistance. The woman flatly refused. The two argued as they walked along the road, until they reached Miaolong Lane. The woman took out two small silver coins and gave them to the lane guard, instructing him to hand them over to Yan and sternly telling him never to come again. She then turned and left without looking back. Yan, considering that he had spent a considerable sum of money on the woman since they had met, including seventy or eighty gold in Shanghai, felt deeply insulted by her actions. Outraged, he took the money and walked out of the lane entrance. In a nearby second-hand store, he bought a barber's razor for ten copper coins, intending to use it to kill the woman and then commit suicide, so that they would perish together. However, he had no suitable opportunity for a while. Until 9:40 AM on the 27th of this month, Yan saw the woman walking alone in Miaolong Lane. He rushed out with the razor and violently slashed at the woman's head and other areas, causing severe injuries to her neck and back. Blood gushed out like a spring, and she collapsed to the ground in pain. Yan, believing that the woman was dead, then cut his own throat, also injuring his windpipe. Blood flowed non-stop, and he fell to the ground in a pool of blood. Upon learning of the incident, the Jing'an Temple police immediately dispatched an ambulance to take the woman to Guangren Hospital for treatment and Yan A'shi to the police hospital. Because Yan's injuries were lighter, after bandaging and applying medicine, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special Court yesterday morning. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, not only charged Yan with attempted murder under Article 284, Section 2 of the Criminal Law but also recounted the above circumstances, saying that Wu Dai'shi's injuries were quite severe and she was currently hospitalized for treatment, so she could not appear in court today and requested a postponement. He then presented the murder weapon as evidence. When questioned, Yan A'shi confessed everything. Judge Wu ordered the defendant to be detained for a seven-day postponement for further investigation and instructed a forensic doctor to examine the injuries.

Shuowen Yao Reprinted 190

The Shuowen Yao, compiled by Ding Jun Fubao in two volumes, is edited using Professor Tu Zhou's method. Its greatest invention is the correction of Xu Xu's preface, changing "the book does not have the word" to "suddenly without the word," based on Zheng Kangcheng's theory of borrowing in haste. Also, Mr. Wu Zhihui changed "ling chang" to "ling liang," both of which are mistakes due to similar forms. Annotation is due to meaning, and borrowing is due to sound. The two are completely different. "Ling liang" is a double sound, so it can be borrowed. For example, "liang qi" can be made "ling qi," and "shi ling qi shou mu" is also. "Liang ren" can be made "ling ren," and "shi wo wu ling ren" is also. Based on this, thousands of years of mistakes can be corrected, which is a major reform for primary school students. The whole book is shallow, easy to understand, step by step into the winning, is the easiest to enter the book of Shuowen. Many schools in Shanghai have adopted it, and the second edition has recently been published. Each volume costs one yuan, and the general distributor is the Medical Book Bureau, 204 Mei Baige Road, Shanghai.
