Impressions of Suiyuan (4) 192

— Xu Zhenhua.

4. The Life Customs of Nomadic Mongolians

The Mongolian people of Suiyuan are divided into six banners under the Iolan Chab League, and seven banners under the Ikchao League, totaling thirteen banners. Additionally, there is one Tumed banner. The people of this banner have lived alongside the Han Chinese in county seats for a long time and have assimilated into Han culture, with no differences in customs and habits. As for the thirteen banners of the Iolan and Ikchao Leagues, they occupy 860,000 square li of land with a population of 200,000. Among them, except for the one Yuanchenhan banner belonging to the Khalkha group, the rest belong to the Ordos group. Therefore, although their life customs are very different from those of the Han Chinese, there are only minor differences between the banners themselves.

Mongolian life is simple and plain, mostly engaged in nomadism, with no knowledge of farming. Dwellings are mostly yurts, circular in shape, with an average circumference of about twenty feet. The dome-shaped structure resembles an umbrella, covered with wool felt. The door faces southeast and is fitted with a wooden frame and two small doors. The yurt can be disassembled and carried, as nomadic life involves moving with the availability of water and pasture, making relocation necessary. The disassembly and assembly of the yurt are mostly done by women, whose movements are agile. It can be disassembled within minutes and erected within half an hour.

Inside the yurt, the floor is covered with wool felt. The stove is in the center, the west side is the men's sitting and sleeping area, and the east side is the women's sitting and sleeping area, with cabinets and water tanks. The northwest corner is reserved for the shrine. At night, there are no beds or bedding, and they sleep in their clothes on the carpet.

Food consists mainly of mutton, fried rice, tea bricks, and cow and sheep milk. Milk is prepared in various ways. It is slowly boiled over a fire, and the coagulated fat layer is taken off to make milk skin and butter. The remaining part is dried in the sun and kneaded into round blocks called sour milk, which tastes both sour and rancid, making it difficult to swallow unless one is accustomed to it. In addition, milk juice mixed with chicken egg whites is dried to make milk tofu, a delicacy for entertaining guests. Milk juice is also stored in jars to ferment, and over time it becomes milk wine.

As for clothing, apart from princes and wealthy households who wear silk and satin, commoners wear cotton cloth, sourced from the Han Chinese. The styles still follow the old Qing Dynasty system, with long robes and belts, with little difference between men and women, except for slight variations in color. Generally, men wear blue or gray, those in mourning wear green, women wear red when young and blue or purple when old, while lamas wear red, yellow, and purple. New clothes are worn until they are worn out, without washing.

Overall, the Mongolians' clothing, food, and housing fail to meet hygiene standards. They also have no medicine when they get sick, so their mortality rate is very high. Furthermore, many Mongolians become lamas; if a family has three sons, one must become a lama. As a result, lamas account for nearly one-third of the total population. The reasons why people like to become lamas include not only the superstition of becoming a Buddha and hoping for happiness in the afterlife, but also three other major reasons: First, to avoid corvée labor, lamas are not managed by princes and are exempt from all duties. Second, due to vanity, lamas have a noble status and do not have to kneel before princes. If there is no lama in a family, they will be ridiculed. Third, lamas lead a leisurely life, and do not have to struggle for food and clothing every day, with most lamas living in 368 temples.

As for Mongolian customs, marriage is also decided by parents through matchmaking. Ordinary men marry at the age of fifteen or sixteen, while women are usually three or four years older than men. The betrothal gifts include cattle, sheep, horses, clothing, coral, and silverware, the amount varying depending on wealth. On the wedding day, the groom first rides a horse to the bride's house to welcome her. The bride's relatives and friends stand outside the door, pretending to refuse to accept him. Then, the bride comes out, mounts a horse, and gallops around her yurt three times. She is then accompanied by a dozen or twenty relatives and friends, riding alongside the groom to his house. The bride dismounts and enters the yurt, pays respects to the stove god, and then one of the male elders of the groom's family holds a bamboo chopstick and separates the bride's hair from the middle to both sides. This is the "separation of hair" ceremony, as Mongolian virgins comb their hair backward, but after marriage, they comb it to the left and right, hanging coral and silver plates as ornaments. Therefore, the "separation of hair" ceremony is an important wedding ritual. After the "separation of hair" ceremony, guests are entertained, and the wedding is completed.

Furthermore, married women can return home at will before having children. After having children, they must wait until they have grown into adults and can ride horses on their own before a lama chants scriptures to allow the mother to return to her parents' home. If the husband and wife are not in harmony, both men and women can file for divorce. However, if a woman files for divorce, she must return all or part of the betrothal gifts to the man's family. After the divorce, both men and women are free to remarry. This is a general outline of the wedding customs.

As for funeral rituals, a few people follow Han customs and use coffins for burial, but most practice cremation and abandonment. Cremation is more common among wealthy families. The method involves cremating the corpse, grinding the ashes into fine powder, mixing it with flour, and kneading it into human shapes, about several inches long, which are then stored in the stupas of large temples. Abandonment is the most common practice, which involves throwing the corpse into the mountains and fields, allowing birds and beasts to peck at it. If the corpse is still intact within three days, it means that the deceased had committed serious sins during their lifetime, and lamas must be invited to chant scriptures to repent for them.

Mongolian life is simple, and apart from weddings and funerals, there are no other special customs. The only holidays of the year are the Kitchen God Festival and the New Year, and the rituals are also very simple. As for other culture and education, there is little to speak of. Apart from lamas who know Tibetan and can chant Buddhist scriptures, less than one in a hundred ordinary people can read. In this era of rapid advancements in world civilization, Mongolian life is still so simple and crude. Unless improvements are sought quickly, it may be difficult to compete for survival with other ethnic groups in the future.

In summary, the above sections show the corruption of Suiyuan society and the hardships of the people. Although it is not easy to suggest relief measures, according to the author's humble opinion, the first priority should be to prohibit opium and rescue women. We must not harm the people by selling their children to buy opium. Once opium and prostitution are eliminated, the fundamental vitality of society will be restored, and then we can talk about suppressing bandits. The method of suppressing bandits should involve setting up village defense corps in the countryside in winter, with practical training. If the people have the power to defend themselves, bandits will not be difficult to eliminate. Once banditry is eliminated and the foundations of rural areas are consolidated, we must then find ways to recover the properties of Catholic churches, and restrict the illegal power of Catholic churches so that they do not harm the villagers. Then, various constructions can be carried out. On the other hand, roads should be built to connect the banners of Inner Mongolia, facilitating the exchange of people between the Han and Mongolian populations. Mongolians should be taught farming methods, and their lifestyles should be improved. Mongolian schools should be established to impart scientific knowledge, dispel Buddhist superstitions, and promote Han-Mongolian marriages to reduce the divide between the ethnic groups. In this way, both Han and Mongolian people can live and work in peace and prosperity, and there is hope for the development of the Northwest. (The End)

Chunqiu

Little Western Paradise 193

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 3: Unable to Understand Salt Tax Regulations, He Pities a Young Girl; Eager to Hear of Hardships, He Visits a Poor Family

That old woman calling out for "Guoguo Kui" said: "Poor people's lives... What's there to see? Just endless suffering." Zhichien said, "I want to know how hard it is. Please sit down, old woman, and let's talk." The old woman did not answer him, but hobbled over to Sister-in-law Hu and asked, "What does this sir do? Is he here to distribute grain? That would be like the sun shining into the house!" Although she spoke in a low voice, Zhichien heard her clearly. He felt that they had great expectations of him, and if he just left like this, he would feel bad. He had originally intended to just come in and take a look and leave, but the mention of "distributing grain" made him freeze in the center of the courtyard, unsure of what to do. Sister-in-law Hu wanted to take this opportunity to test his abilities to make connections. She narrowed her eyes, looked at Zhichien, and said with a smile to the old woman, "Didn't I say that I was going to find someone for my niece? There are guests living in Little Western Paradise who are interested, but nothing is certain yet. This sir..." She lowered her voice and whispered something to the old woman. Zhichien could see that this situation was embarrassing, and his face turned red. He thought quickly and realized that he couldn't be ambiguous here. He said, "Sister-in-law, I've heard a little about your relatives' affairs. I have good intentions and want to advise you not to do this." Zhichien said this hastily to clarify that he wasn't there to look at the girl, but he didn't have any other solutions for them. However, Sister-in-law Hu continued to misunderstand, always thinking that he had come because he admired Yueying. So, she wanted to ask him for a second feasible solution. (52)

Vegetable Seedling Flood 194

— Gao Jinyu

The transition from August to September – the vegetable seedling flood – is an important season for farmers along the Puzuo Dike. They hastily cut away the withered vines of watermelons and golden melons that had provided the city dwellers with relief from the summer heat, and painstakingly used hoes to meticulously till the soil, creating neat and orderly drainage ditches. The seedbeds were leveled like whetstones and evenly fertilized, like a beautifully dressed woman who, having come out of her door, turns back to reapply her makeup. In this way, perhaps after rain and moisture, the soil hardens, and then another effort is made to refine it. Then, they scatter seeds of long-stemmed cabbage and snow cabbage, treading lightly. Within three or four days, sprouts emerge distinctly.

Protecting vegetable seedlings is as painstaking as nurturing silkworms. From sprouting to three or four inches high, over the course of a month, not only must there be timely rain and sunshine, but also daily, even combing, and weeding out aphids. The biggest enemy of vegetable seedlings is the submerged grub, followed by the biting grub. If biting grubs are found on the vegetable seedlings, they can be killed with pesticide powder without any problem. But if submerged grubs swarm across the fields, they are like a bone-deep sore, and the vegetable seedlings can only wither and fade away every day, until they collapse.

The clear moonlight of the Mid-Autumn Festival shines through the flat, green vegetable seedlings, like graceful goddesses, wandering back and forth between the embroidered fields. After offering sacrifices to the moon and burning incense, the farmers all wear joyful expressions, indicating that the short-term labor will bring them several times more harvest than other crops.

However, the dike farmers, who are not increasing in number, cannot escape the sad atmosphere of rural decline. After a few days of hope, their beloved vegetable seedlings are almost entirely overturned by submerged grubs. In addition to the labor of blood and sweat, they also lose the capital they invested in hiring workers, fertilizer, and pesticides. Sadly, their capital is all borrowed from high-interest loans, and of course, the land rent cannot be repaid.

Sketch of Slaughtering a Cow 195

— Yi Zhen

People filled the bridge and stood below it. A disturbed atmosphere enveloped these people.

A young man led a pair of thin, old, and tired cows, slowly, slowly, from a dilapidated thatched hut towards the big stone bridge. The old cows seemed to know that a great disaster was about to befall them, and they refused to move their hind legs. So the young man angrily pulled the rope tightly. The cows couldn't bear the pain and continued to walk forward. Slowly, slowly.

They walked onto the big stone bridge. Thwack! Another young man suddenly raised a large wooden stick and struck the thin cow's leg hard. The old cow collapsed! A long and sorrowful cry.

Then two young men and four strong men ran up. They deftly tied the old cow's thin legs tightly. Ah! A thin rope severed all the cow's freedom. Then, sharp, large stones were continuously slammed onto the cow's massive head. The old cow shook its legs, which had lost their freedom, and endured. A little bit of fresh blood flowed from its wounded mouth, and drops of hot tears dripped from its lifeless eyes. The muted cry was long and sorrowful.

Finally, the sorrowful cry slowly weakened, weakened. Until it stopped...

Two young men dragged the cow's legs and threw it onto the empty ground at the foot of the bridge. Two sharp and gleaming knives first cut off the toes that had walked thousands of miles for people! Then, they chopped off its massive head... Fresh blood stained the yellowing grass.

Ah! A lifetime of hard work! Only to be rewarded with such an end!

Snippets 196

— (Retired Farmer)

Some people may call these words cold-blooded.

A child used a bamboo pole to hit a crab. The crab became angry, raised its two big claws to resist, and clamped the bamboo pole tightly. The child then caught the crab.

If the crab had known to be sensible, not clamp the bamboo pole with its claws, cultivated deep patience, and not become angry at all, there would have been no reason for the child to catch it. Suppressing anger and calming wrath is the way for a wise person to protect themselves!

The Fragrant Drifting Record of the Imperial Palace 197

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

The demeanor of officials should always be more generous than that of ordinary soldiers. Although they generally lowered their heads and knelt, their upper bodies were still upright, making them appear more dignified than those prostrating like toads. However, the attire of these officials and soldiers was uniformly neat and beautiful: they looked like two rows of moving lanterns, specially set up to welcome the Empress Dowager. We sat in yellow or red sedan chairs between these two rows of moving lanterns, slowly passing by: plus, the eunuchs who carried the chairs were all dressed in extremely gorgeous palace attire: therefore, the scenery of this comedy was extraordinarily colorful and dazzling! At that time, the sun was at its peak, and the light was very strong, shining on these red and green colors, making our procession as dazzling as a long rainbow, which everyone who saw it couldn't help but stop to watch.

Although the colors of our team were so rich and beautiful, in spirit, they were still very solemn and quiet, almost without any sound. Even the little eunuchs carrying the sedan chairs didn't make much noise. This was not because their footsteps were too light, but because of the half-wet yellow sand spread on the ground, which covered their footsteps entirely. In such a quiet atmosphere, we sat stiffly in the sedan chairs, resembling the clay and wood statues, or the characters in the historical paintings painted on tapestries or oil paintings, who suddenly came back to life due to some strange magic, lined up, and walked on the street.

In Fengtian, such a grand and imposing ceremony might not be seen once in hundreds of years: this time, it happened to allow those officials to attend in person. All ordinary people were not allowed to watch. (162)

Stinginess with Style 198

Boat Girls of Huzhou 199

— Yan Beguang

With yellow chrysanthemums blooming and red maples dyed with rouge, it is the perfect time of year for pleasant outings. If we travel to Huzhou, the scenery of mountains and lakes can make people's eyes wander and their hearts soar. For famous scenic spots such as Baique, Yunchao, and Daoyan, it is necessary to use boats to travel through the waterways, just as hiring boats is necessary to visit the Rain Tower in Jiaxing.

Every day, when the east just barely shows the white of fish bellies, they get up and wash, appearing very neat and tidy. Their clothing is mostly made of black Huzhou crepe. Promoting the local product of Huzhou crepe is worthy of praise during the Women's National Goods Year. But their bound feet have undergone a great deal of artistic care. A pair of black satin embroidered leather-soled slippers is truly spotless. After getting on the boat, familiar tourists can sometimes see the various colors of nail polish on their toes, and their fleshy legs are smeared with talcum powder.

In the hazy morning mist, the riverfront of the inn is their market for greeting tourists. The speaking skills and tones are purely Huzhou dialect, which is interesting and elegant.

After the tourists board the boat, they untie the cable and set sail, and the rippling waves can clear people's minds. When rocking to remote harbor, tourists can ask them to sing new-style songs like "Peach Blossom River" or "Beauty Talk." When rocking the boat, the swaying of their willow waists is as soft as a dancer's waist!

When it's time to eat lunch, they prepare delicious boat dishes, anchor in the middle of the lake, and they can hold the wine pot and drink with you. But the tour fee is not expensive. If three or four people travel together, it can be considered an economical trip.

General Mobilization of Laughter

Impatient People 200

— Sha Yu

Mr. Zhang, who has always been impatient, went to a noodle shop to eat noodles. After sitting down, he had just told the waiter what kind of noodles he wanted, before the waiter could even turn around, he had already started urging the noodles to come quickly. In less than a minute, he had been banging the table and hitting the bench, making a lot of noise. It was only with great difficulty that he saw the waiter carrying a bowl of steaming hot meat noodles, walking towards him. Mr. Zhang quickly raised his chopsticks, preparing to eat. But the waiter replied righteously, "Guests, after you finish eating the noodles, the bowl has to be taken away and washed before it can be used to serve noodles to other people. But I am also an impatient person, and I can't wait for you to finish eating the noodles and take the bowl away, so I dumped the noodles upstairs, so I can take this bowl and do other business." Mr. Zhang was even more angry when he heard this, but he couldn't find a reason to refute the waiter. He had to throw down his chopsticks and angrily ran home, telling his wife what had happened, and then said, "Aren't you angry? What face do I have to live in this world? I must commit suicide!" His wife agreed, "It's good that you commit suicide, but I will inevitably remarry after you commit suicide. I am also an impatient person, please find a husband for me first, and then commit suicide." While Mr. and Mrs. Zhang were talking, suddenly there was a loud crash, bricks and stones flew, and a hole opened in the wall next door, and someone crawled over. He shouted loudly, "Sister-in-law, don't be impatient, marry me instead!" He turned to Mr. Zhang and said, "I am also an impatient person, so I don't have time to go out the front door and come in the front door, which is so far away, so I had to break through the wall and crawl over."

Roasted Meat 201

One day, Mr. Wang suddenly carried a piece of lean and fat meat home and gave it to his wife, instructing her: "Roast this meat plainly. It must be roasted until it is tender, so that it tastes good. Do you understand?" His wife pouted and said, "Why don't I understand? You don't have to nag." After Mr. Wang heard this, he went out to do errands. At twelve o'clock, he returned home, preparing to eat. As soon as he stepped through the door, he saw his wife covered in sweat, wearing short clothes, rushing out from inside, panting and saying, "Tired to death! Tired to death! You want to get rid of meat, causing me to sweat so much!" Mr. Wang asked, "Is it roasted?" His wife said, "Almost! It's not very rotten yet, your meat is stringy and it's not easy to get rid of!" After speaking, she went inside and picked out a black thing and threw it to Mr. Wang, "See, isn't it still very rotten?" Mr. Wang took a look and the piece of meat was like a piece of mud, no longer tasty. Angrily, he laughed and said, "How exactly did you roast this meat?" His wife said, "You said 'get rid of meat', so I used a rope to lash the meat and 'get rid' of it inside, and have already 'got rid' of it so much sweat." After Mr. Wang heard this, he was speechless with anger, after a long while, he said: "What I was saying was roast meat, that is to clean the meat, and roast it on the fire, I wasn't telling you to 'get rid' of it like that!" A day later, Mr. Wang bought tofu and went home, but before he even left, his wife had already chased him out and said: "The method you taught me is good! Go and see, go and see." Mr. Wang was confused, and rushed to the stove to take a look, and saw that a few blocks of tofu had already been turned into a white, greasy tofu pulp by his wife.

Humorous Thief 202

When Mr. Li came out of the cinema, he found that his wallet in his pocket had been stolen. He hurriedly looked around and saw a disheveled person walking away quickly, so he ran over and grabbed the person. The person looked at Mr. Li and said anxiously, "Sir, I didn't steal your wallet." Mr. Li thought if he didn't steal the wallet, how would he know about the stolen wallet? Without saying a word, he handed the person over to the police. Sure enough, the police searched the thief and found his lost wallet. The police asked Mr. Li how he discovered that he had lost his wallet, so Mr. Li vividly described the situation of the stolen wallet. But the thief interrupted him and said, "Sir, what you said is completely wrong. I didn't do it that way, I stole your wallet like this." As the thief spoke, he even made gestures, so Mr. Li couldn't help but laugh, the police also laughed, and the people watching around also laughed. But when they stopped laughing, the thief had already slipped away while they were laughing.

Education News

Recent Key Points of Improvements for Colleges and Above by the Ministry of Education (Part 2) 203

1. Streamlining Departments:

In the past, the establishment of departments in universities often disregarded faculty and facilities, leading to arbitrary setups that affected other departments and rarely achieved good results. Moreover, many departments in various universities were redundant, especially in Shanghai and Beiping. Taking Beiping as an example, in the 20th year of the Republic (1931), there were twelve public and private universities and independent colleges, divided into more than thirty colleges (departments in independent colleges are considered as colleges) and more than one hundred and thirty departments. By college type, there were the following: College of Liberal Arts, College of Law as follows, College of Science - 7, with Agriculture, Engineering, and Medicine having one or two colleges each. By department, among the one hundred and thirty-plus departments, there were ten each of Chinese Literature and Economics, nine each of Political Science and Foreign Literature, seven each of Law and Physics, six each of History, Philosophy, and Mathematics, five each of Education and Sociology, and Chemistry, four each of Biology and Psychology, and two each of Geography and Music. In addition, each of the other departments had one or two. The situation of redundant departments in Shanghai universities was similar to that in Beiping. Other provinces and cities had fewer redundant departments. However, the Ministry of Education ordered to merge, reduce, or stop admitting new students in stages. For example, the Department of Philosophy and Education of the Women's College of Liberal Arts of Beiping University was abolished, the Departments of Chinese Literature, History, and Geography were merged into the Department of Liberal Arts and History, and the College of Commerce and the College of Law were merged and renamed the College of Law and Commerce, with the establishment of the Department of Commerce, International Trade, Business Administration, and Transportation Management, which were not allowed to recruit new students from this year. The Department of Sociology of Beiping Normal University was abolished, the Department of Law of Tsinghua University was abolished, and the College of Education of Jinan University was abolished. The original departments were merged into the Department of Education and incorporated into the College of Liberal Arts. The College of Law was abolished, and the original students were transferred to the College of Law of the National Central University to study. The Department of Sociology of Henan University stopped recruiting new students, and the Department of Civil Engineering was abolished. The Departments of Chinese Literature and History were merged into the Department of Liberal Arts and History. The College of Law, except for the Department of Economics, no longer recruits students. After the existing students of the Departments of Law and Political Science graduate, the Department of Economics will be merged into the College of Liberal Arts. Shanxi College of Education and Shanxi College of Law were both merged into Shanxi University. The College of Education of Sichuan University was abolished and changed to the Department of Education and incorporated into the College of Liberal Arts. The Departments of Mathematics and Physics of Anhui University were merged into the Department of Mathematics and Physics. The College of Law was abolished, and the original students were either transferred to other schools or changed departments. Hebei College of Law and Commerce stopped recruiting students altogether. Other schools with redundant departments and lack of faculty and facilities, and the departments that were unable to develop, were all ordered to draft merger plans and submit them to the Ministry for approval. The purpose is to completely reduce redundancy and adapt to actual needs, so that the human and financial resources of various schools are concentrated on special enrichment and development.

2. Enriching Equipment:

According to the statistics of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), the new equipment expenditure of colleges and above in the country was about 6.4 million yuan, 200,000 yuan. It can be seen that the annual new equipment expenditure of various schools in recent years is about 6.4 million yuan, which is undoubtedly a considerable progress. Among the 6.4 million yuan of new equipment expenditure in the 20th year of the Republic (1931), library fees accounted for 17%, and instrument, specimen, and machine fees accounted for 26%, totaling 43%. The remaining 57% was mostly for construction, repairs, and school furniture and sundries. Among the more than 6.2 million yuan of new equipment expenditure in the 21st year of the Republic (1932), library fees accounted for 18%. Among the more than 6.5 million yuan of new equipment expenditure recently, library fees accounted for 18.8%. Instrument, specimen, and machine fees accounted for 31.8%. Among the more than 6.5 million yuan of new equipment expenditure recently, library fees accounted for 32%. If we compare the three years, the recent library fees have increased by about 2% compared to the 20th year of the Republic (1931), and by about 0.2% compared to the 21st year of the Republic (1932). Instrument, specimen, and machine fees have increased by about 5.6% compared to the 20th year of the Republic (1931), and by about 0.2% compared to the 21st year of the Republic (1932). It can be seen that various schools have indeed made considerable increases in equipment such as books and instruments. However, this increase refers to the whole. Individually, many still do not meet the statutory standards, especially private ones. According to the regulations, the equipment expenditure of universities should account for at least 15% of the recurring expenditure, and the administrative expenditure should not exceed 10%. Therefore, colleges and above should strive to reduce administrative expenditure and increase equipment expenditure. In addition to ordering various schools to enrich equipment such as instruments and books, the Ministry of Education has approved the subsidy fee for private colleges and above this year, with equipment fee accounting for 81.5%. This is the meaning of special attention to equipment.

Subsidy Fees for Private Colleges and Above to be Issued Monthly 204

The Ministry of Education Formulates Payment Methods

(Nanjing, 29th Dispatch) The Ministry of Education has formulated the payment methods for subsidy fees for private colleges and above. On the 29th, it issued a notice to private colleges and above to comply with and handle. 1. Private colleges and above that have applied for subsidies but have not submitted the entire budget for this year should submit the budget as soon as possible before receiving the subsidy. 2. All private colleges and above that have been approved to receive subsidy fees should submit a detailed budget of the various expenses subsidized to the Ministry for approval after receiving the subsidy notice from the Ministry. All those subsidized for equipment fees should also submit a detailed list of the detailed names, uses, exact numbers, prices, and purchase locations of the items for approval. The original budget of the subsidized colleges or departments must not be reduced. 3. All those subsidized for professorship fees must, before receiving the subsidy, submit the names, qualifications, salaries, and subjects taught by the teachers of special education hired by the subsidized schools to the Ministry for approval. 4. All teachers who are engaged in special education must not concurrently serve as teachers or positions outside the school. 5. The subsidized special professorship fee is set at 4,000 yuan per seat this year, and the minimum monthly salary must not be less than 280 yuan. When there is a surplus in the aforementioned professorship fee, all the funds will be used to supplement the equipment fee for the subject. 6. Lecture fees are limited to the purchase of specialized machines, machine specimens, models, instruments, medicines, and books. 7. The subsidy fee will be issued monthly by the Ministry of Education. 8. After receiving the subsidy fee, each school should immediately fill out the receipt and submit it to the Ministry of Education for transfer to the audit agency for verification. The receipt should be signed and sealed by the principal and the person in charge of the subsidized college or department at the same time. Legal receipts must be submitted for equipment fees, and salary receipts must be submitted for education fees. The aforementioned receipts must be submitted at least once every three months. 9. All those who fail to prepare a budget or report expenses or fail to submit the matters that should be reported in accordance with these measures may not be issued the subsidy fee, or the issuance may be suspended halfway. 10. These measures shall be implemented from the date of distribution by the Ministry of Education.

(Nanjing, 29th Dispatch) The Ministry of Education believes that the matters under the jurisdiction of the National Academic Work Advisory Office and the educational administrative organs of various provinces and cities should be connected and carried out. On the 29th, it issued the regulations of the office to the educational departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities for information.

Judging Procedures for the National Elementary School Mandarin Competition 208

The National Mandarin Education Promotion Association founded the National Elementary School Mandarin Competition. The Ministry of Education has issued a notice. The judging procedures of the association are divided into three types: preliminary selection, reselection, and final selection. The review meeting passed yesterday. The details are extracted below: 1. Preliminary Selection: The competition papers from public and private elementary schools in various provinces, cities, and counties across the country have been collected by the education departments and bureaus of various joint provinces and cities according to the notice issued by the Ministry of Education. By November 1st of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934), two excellent papers from each group will be selected and sent to the office of the National Mandarin Education Promotion Association on Ping Le Li, Xizang Road, Shanghai. Upon receipt of the papers, the association will immediately send them to the National Elementary School Mandarin Competition Committee of the association (hereinafter referred to as the Competition Committee). The Competition Committee will first register them, then paste the judging scoring sheet on the cover of the papers, and forward them to the reselection judging directors of each group in the order of receipt for reselection. 2. Reselection: Upon receiving the numbered papers, the reselection judging directors of each group will immediately meet with the judges of the group, review them in turn, and determine the scores for each item, which will be entered in the judging scoring sheet. Then, the directors of each group will summarize the scores, sign or affix a seal, and submit them to the Competition Committee of the association. Upon receiving the papers assessed and scored by the reselection judges of each group, the Competition Committee will submit the twenty papers with the highest scores from each group to the judging chairman for final selection. 3. Final Selection: Upon receiving the best papers from the reselection of each group, the judging chairman will immediately meet with the final selection judges, review them separately, rank them, and indicate the ranking on the judging scoring sheet. The judging chairman will affix a seal and return them to the Competition Committee of the association. The Competition Committee will then submit them to the association for binding into a book and submit them to the Ministry of Education for the issuance of awards.

Xu Wancheng's "Collection of Discussions on Life Problems" Published 217

"Collection of Discussions on Life Problems" is published by Longwen Bookstore in Dananmen, Shanghai. The author, Mr. Xu Wancheng, spent three years conducting life problem tests in major newspapers, which caused a nationwide sensation. Young people responded enthusiastically. He also conducted tests on the three major problems of studying, exploring a career, and love in this newspaper. He is the first person in China to discuss practical life problems and conduct tests in newspapers, and to compile the thoughts of the public into a book. The whole book is divided into three parts, with nearly 300,000 words. The first part is written by Xu himself, and its main points include: 1. What is the meaning of life? 2. A word to the young people who are studying. 3. A word to the young people who are choosing a career and serving. 4. A word to the young people who are in love and getting married. 5. How to cultivate a happy life and build a rational family life. 6. How should young people strive to create? 7. How should young people transform society and transform the country? 8. Where should I go with regard to modern trends of thought and doctrines? 9. How should I deal with the current social situation? etc. The middle part is the statistics of the answers to life problems sought in major newspapers. The lower part is more than 60 micro-essays, and the article "My Life" has more than 20 celebrities from all walks of life writing about their personal outlook on life, which is quite practical. It is heard that every scholar who purchases the collection will be given a book title praising the youth, with inscriptions from Cai Yuanpei, Jiang Menglin, Ma Junwu, Li Shicen, and more than 40 others, compiled and printed like a diploma, which can be used as a motto. The price is two yuan per copy. Those who answered the questions will be given a 40% discount coupon, which is valid only when purchasing from Longwen Bookstore, Dananmen, Shanghai.

Page 15

Free Talk

Words and Deeds 235

— Zhou Muzhai

Those who are sick and do not take medicine often encounter traditional Chinese medicine. Those with mediocre talent often encounter mediocre people. Those with sufficient talent, if they do not do good, will do evil, and will never be content to be mediocre. Doing good is beneficial to others, and doing evil only cares about oneself. Those with talent would rather do evil. The more talent one has, the more ability one has to do evil. Those with good ability, one sees their good, but not their evil. Evil is disguised by good. Therefore, Lao Zhuang advocated eliminating sages and eliminating knowledge.

However, Lao Zhuang were also extremely intelligent people. The Daodejing and the Zhuangzi reveal the secrets of the human world with extreme thoroughness. Logically, sin should be reduced. But from another point of view, it is no different from teaching a monkey to climb a tree. It cannot be reduced, but instead is encouraged. This may be the pain that they spoke of and then wanted not to speak of. If words were exchanged for actions, it could become the greatest treachery.

And these two things are like explaining oneself through one's own actions, like understanding the principle of the curtain, and also covering oneself with a layer of curtain. Clever people will say, "Today's me is not yesterday's me." With a flip of the tongue, they transform themselves. In fact, they have also removed the curtain themselves, and then put on another layer of curtain, or simply revealed their original form.

Wushan 236

— Yin Guang

In the twilight veil, the ship slowly anchored at Wushan. The passengers had already strolled onto the deck, some holding pipes, some yawning, some paying attention to the teahouse attendants' directions. Everyone was constantly sending curious gazes towards the riverbank, where the castle was located, as if they could find some eye-catching architecture and lively streets.

However, here, what entered people's eyes was nothing but a patch of glaring desolation.

The city was perched on top of a not-very-tall earthen mountain, low and pitiful. It seemed that its deliberate squatting high up was not to show the characteristics of a mountain city, but to let people appreciate its desolation and backwardness. That is to say, in the continuous disturbances, under poor natural conditions, a town, although located on an important river line, is how it is on the verge of dying.

The observers shook their heads and already showed a dispirited expression. They didn't seem to feel any interest at all. A young man who looked like he was just out of the house stared and muttered to himself:

"Oh my, is that what it's like after all this talk?" He even gave a wry smile from his nose.

Many people went back to their berths. From the murky river surface, three or four grayish-brown rowboats floated lazily. But there was no shouting to sell food, and no sound of soliciting customers. It seemed that the purpose of those boat owners was simply to rush over and share a little of the so-called excitement of the human world. However, because of these scattered embellishments, the river surface seemed even colder.

"Is anyone going ashore?" Those who stayed on the deck asked each other listlessly.

"Come to the back, come to the back." Only then did the small boats row towards the stern of the steamboat with more effort.

"Don't delay, don't cause trouble!" The soldiers escorting the boat warned each boarding guest.

When I was in a dilapidated rowboat with a tea attendant and two small-time opium merchants, the night had already gradually deepened. A kind of gloomy feeling surrounded us. However, although the place where we were moored was still in the middle of this long gorge, the gloom was the desolation of Guanghan and did not carry the depth and solemnity that should be in the mountain gorges. Because the mountains that had rushed from the upper reaches seemed to have suddenly collapsed here, leaving only some earthen hills and small mountains, and a riverbank piled with rubble.

"Hey, Fangfang," the boatman pointed to the boat's hull with an empty wine bottle and shouted, "You should pay some money to fix it."

"Easy to say, fix it..."

As if criticizing the accuser's lack of awareness, the boatman didn't finish speaking, and then lazily turned his head to take care of his oar.

This was an old man in his fifties, with a sandy white beard, a dark and wrinkled face. He lazily wielded his dilapidated oar inlaid with new wood, his waist stretching and bending, his eyes half-closed, as if his work was not for food, but to casually dispose of his time that had long been pawned. Due to the tea attendant's intensified urging, before long, the boat had already landed.

"Old man," I asked the boatman, who now only had to take care of the boat's direction, "I heard that bandits have appeared again?"

"Yes, they're making trouble again. The army only left a few days ago."

Then the two opium merchants shifted their bodies and began to show off their erudition. In such a conversation, the boat docked. Then, walking over a sandy beach mixed with gravel, walking up the sloping path, we entered the desolate county town.

However, saying it was a county town, its size and liveliness were actually disproportionate, even compared with the market towns in other regions. And it still maintained the old appearance of all small towns, narrow streets, low houses, bamboo poles for drying clothes and firewood waiting to be split across the streets. A little boy, holding up his pants with one hand, and holding a rattan whip-like tow rope in the other, cried and ran towards several running piglets.

On the steps of several teahouses, there were stoves and equipment for cooking opium. The two opium merchants went to discuss their business in a serious manner, and the tea attendant disappeared under the eaves of a dark hole. And I, who was already very disappointed at that time, wandered alone in the market until I gathered my companions, the opium merchants and the tea attendant, at the city gate.

We stepped on the steep return path again, but I was still oppressed by a kind of restless mood.

"Mr. Zhang, look up!" the tea attendant suddenly greeted me in a laughing tone, while turning on his electric torch.

Following the direction of the light, I looked up at the top of the electric pole on the side of the road: hanging on it were three terrible things that had lost their blood color. But I did not panic as my companions had hoped. After staring for a while, I returned to my own thoughts.

When the rowboat was approaching the steamboat, we encountered trouble with the soldiers escorting the boat.

This was in the autumn of 1931. Early the next morning, the boat entered the Wuxia Gorge, with its towering cliffs on both sides.

Honest and Sincere People 237

— Bi Bing

Luo Fu is an honest and sincere person; at least, he is confident in that himself. Although Luo Fu has lived in Shanghai for eight or nine years, and although Luo Fu has traveled to Hong Kong, Macau, Tianjin, Beiping, Hankou, Qingdao, Jinan, Nanjing, Jiujiang, and other commercial ports within the Chinese territory besides Shanghai, and although Luo Fu has experienced many different types of jobs, such as teacher, contributor, political work in the military, and railway inspector, and although Luo Fu has also experienced various different ways of life, such as renting a room for twelve or thirteen yuan, and being so poor that he has nowhere to stand, perhaps no one will believe it when I say that Luo Fu can still be said to be an honest and sincere person now.

Luo Fu believes that he has a very deep understanding of worldly affairs and human relationships. Whether the relationship with someone is long or short, Luo Fu believes that he can judge good and evil, wisdom and foolishness clearly. However, there are many people who think that Luo Fu does not understand worldly affairs and human relationships and treat him as an easy person to bully. And Luo Fu really is bullied and played with once, twice, three times... to increase his experience.

"This person has no hope; he will always be a drifter. He doesn't know the rules of being a person at all." Many people, after bullying and playing with Luo Fu, turn around and seem to blame him with good intentions.

………………

Luo Fu, when blamed, cannot say half a word in rebuttal, because the current society… especially Shanghai or other cities, simply doesn't need honest and sincere people. Honest and sincere people simply cannot stand in this kind of society. Luo Fu, when blamed, of course, cannot rebut others except to endure and blame himself.

Sometimes, because the wounds inflicted by being played with and bullied are too deep, and the lessons are too many, Luo Fu also wants to cheer up and be a person… naturally a modern person. A person who adapts to modern society, a person who can speak lies and deceive; in this way, perhaps he can also stand in this society.

"Hey! Are you going to Guangdong today?"

"No! I'm going to Hankou tomorrow."

"I heard that you have been very close to Mr. Huang lately. I think you will be successful in the near future."

"I don't know Mr. Huang. That person is very good at using methods; you must not be fooled by him."

Such a reply, knowingly affirming the truth yet denying it, others may think that Luo Fu is really good at being a person now and can speak hypocritical and deceptive words. So, in their hearts, they implicitly express admiration for Luo Fu, believing that he is a teachable son. However, only God will believe that when Luo Fu deliberately says these replies, knowingly affirming the truth yet denying it, because he is too deeply stimulated, Luo Fu's inner pain is unbearable, and it exceeds several times the severe trauma he suffers from treating people with a sincere heart, only to be played with by others using hypocritical and deceptive means, because this is not only deceiving others but perhaps also deceiving oneself. Why do I have to be hypocritical and deceptive in what I do and say to people! Thinking like this, perhaps Luo Fu will cry and kneel before the person who has heard Luo Fu's hypocritical and deceptive words, begging him to forgive him.

"What's going on with this; is he a lunatic!"

However, others are, after all, others. Others, after hearing Luo Fu's hypocritical and deceptive words, may not be able to realize that they are fake and think that Luo Fu is really treating people with a sincere heart. Perhaps they do realize that they are lies, but they admire Luo Fu's pain in being a human being. But now, instead of waiting for Luo Fu to speak the truth, and frankly confessing and repenting, they belittle him and think that Luo Fu's actions are inhuman. As a result, Luo Fu's sincere repentance is despised by others.

"This person really has no hope; he might as well commit suicide."

Although no one says so to his face, someone advocates this behind his back. Afterwards, when meeting Luo Fu, others will reveal contemptuous expressions or keep him at a distance out of respect.

Therefore, Luo Fu's experience of worldly affairs and human relationships, although rich, is ultimately useless to apply. If applied, it can only backfire and ruin his reputation as an honest and sincere person. For this reason, Luo Fu dares not tell even half a lie when dealing with people, and even if he accidentally says one or two wrong words, he has to quickly correct them, lest others think that he is playing tricks.

The honest and sincere person becomes even more deserving of his name, showing his honesty and sincerity.

As a result, Luo Fu's friends are only children or teenagers who are just beginning to understand worldly affairs because these people, like Luo Fu, treat people with honesty and sincerity. Birds of a feather flock together. Only then can they be in harmony with each other. However, when those children or teenagers grow up and understand worldly affairs, they will also treat people with hypocrisy and deception. Then, at that time, Luo Fu will be played with, bullied, and despised by those children or teenagers, and Luo Fu will become estranged from these former young children whom he regarded as children and teenagers. So, those who associate with him change to some new children and teenagers. However, when the future days arrive, those second batch (?) of children and teenagers become young gentlemen, and after understanding worldly affairs and human relationships, Luo Fu will only be able to get along with the third batch (?) of children and teenagers. Such a formula, the relay race of changing generals, has now been going on for eight or nine years. In these days, there has already been a fifth batch (?) of children and teenagers who have become the young gentlemen of today's society. However, Luo Fu is still not progressing. Luo Fu now can only get along with the sixth batch of children and teenagers.

Luo Fu will never be able to comprehend the most important lesson in life and society! Worldly affairs and human relationships will bear the nickname given to the honest and sincere person, all the way until the end of his life.

Nanyang Street One 238

— Black Infant

Flat and solid, paved with a layer of asphalt. No trees on either side, no tall, magnificent buildings. All are two or three-story buildings, and not very neat: some are old, and some are modern buildings. But you can probably tell that Chinese people will always love to do their business in old shops.

Those facing east prop up the white cloth awnings before the sun rises, to prevent the tropical sun from scorching them after an hour. On the cloth, the store names are painted in two or even three languages: you can imagine how different Chinese characters and Latin letters look side by side.

Gradually, there were more and more people on the street, and more and more cars. The people are very mixed: if you stand in the center of the road where the Malay police station is for twenty or thirty minutes, the following different kinds of humans will be displayed in front of you:

Yellow-faced Chinese and Japanese. Blue-eyed Germans, Dutch, British, Portuguese, Americans... Black Africans, Javanese... (You won't be able to tell them apart unless you have knowledge of ethnology.)

In the cars, sit the descendants of those who became rich from rubber plantations during the European War: when they think back to those good old days, they shake their heads and sigh. Carriages seem to be a special existence here, arousing the curiosity of some newcomers, who stare intently at the horses that set off and run forward with their four hooves, and at the coachman. Bicycles come and go in groups: sometimes you see young women riding them. Their skill and naturalness in driving are surprising, aren't they?

The elementary school students, carrying schoolbags, walk to school, smiling and rushing forward with a whoosh. If you walk in front of them, they will catch up with you in a while.

Children who grow up in Nanyang are always lively and lovely. Their active and energetic character teaches them to fight once a day. You may be surprised at the Malay police: why don't they interfere when they see children fighting? But, if you wait for ten minutes, the loser will obediently follow the person and walk their way.

The Javanese carts pushing "Ice Cream" and lemonade also appeared on the street, the bells ringing. Some people, regardless of whether they are thirsty or not, throw down three or five copper coins and have a cup of sweet iced water to drink. The Javanese, with a face full of beards, wearing gauze, slowly pushes and turns away from there.

Calligraphy Square (5) 239

— Why

Seeing me hesitating and unable to choose, he helped me flip through it for a long time. Then, without even toasting the paper, without even taking off his boots, he helped me grind ink and cut paper. Because he was afraid of cutting the paper wrong, he carefully measured it again and again, folded it again and again. After the paper was cut, he used his fingers to draw fingerprints on it, and used his mother's powder to draw crosses on it, constantly saying:

You must write evenly and neatly, arrange the positions well, and especially write the couplets in straight lines, and avoid writing them upside down, crookedly...

A serious light was visible on his face, his wrinkled skin tightened and relaxed, constantly changing shape, and his lips seemed to be distorted by the stimulation of excessive excitement. While tightly clamping the new ink that he had specially bought, with his skinny hands, he glanced over the encyclopedia wrapped in a black cover, his mouth opening and closing, as if chanting in a low voice.

I also bought a new goat hair brush, a real calligraphy square brush, all for Uncle Zhang's sake!

Everything was arranged properly. Afterwards, as if opening an exhibition, my father went to invite several gentlemen from the neighborhood to watch me write. These people were all first-class figures in the village, engaging in iron-clad fraud and all kinds of evil. They didn't do any serious work all year round, but they were dressed exquisitely and ate exquisitely. They were not only despicable and disgusting, but also extremely arrogant. I have always disliked these benevolent officials, but my father invited them to watch me write, like supervisors, so my aversion to them increased even more.

I heard these parasites, who seemed to know everything and were shameless, constantly praising me:

Congratulations, congratulations, you have such a son, you are really extremely happy!

Several of them could not hide their envy and jealousy, and said:

Face! Uncle Zhang's face, what else is there to say?

Page 16

Education News

Key Points for Recent Improvement of Colleges and Universities by the Ministry of Education (2) 240

1. Reorganizing departments and faculties: In the past, when universities reorganized departments and faculties, they often set them up arbitrarily regardless of faculty and equipment, which affected other departments and faculties, and few achieved good results. Moreover, there were many overlapping departments and faculties in various schools, especially in Shanghai and Peiping. Taking Peiping as an example, in the 20th year of the Republic, there were a total of twelve public and private universities and independent colleges, divided into more than 30 colleges (the departments in independent colleges were regarded as colleges), and more than 130 departments. In terms of colleges, there were liberal arts colleges and law colleges, seven science colleges, and one or two colleges of agriculture, engineering, and medicine. In terms of departments, among the more than 130 departments, there were ten Chinese literature departments and economics departments, nine political science departments and foreign literature departments, seven law departments and physics departments, six history departments, philosophy departments, and mathematics departments, five education departments, sociology departments, and chemistry departments, four biology departments and psychology departments, and three geography departments and music departments. In addition, there were one or two departments in each of the other departments. The situation of overlapping departments and faculties in major universities in Shanghai was similar to that in Peiping. The duplication of departments and faculties in other provinces and cities was less common, but the Ministry of Education separately ordered them to be reduced or merged, or to stop recruiting new students and end them in stages. The philosophy and education departments of the Women's Liberal Arts College of Peiping University were abolished, the Chinese literature and history departments were merged into the literature and history department, and the business school and law school were merged and renamed the law and business school, with the business department, international trade, business administration, and transportation management departments. From this year onwards, no new students will be recruited. The sociology department of Peiping Normal University was abolished, the law department of Tsinghua University was abolished, the education college of Jinan University was abolished, and the original departments were merged into the education department and merged into the liberal arts college. The law school was abolished, and the original students were transferred to the law school of National Central University. The sociology department of Henan University stopped recruiting new students, the civil engineering department was abolished, the Chinese literature department and the history department were merged into the literature and history department, and the law school, except for the economics department, no longer enrolled students. After the existing students of the law and political science departments have finished their studies, the economics department will be merged into the liberal arts college. Shanxi Education College and Shanxi Law College were both merged into Shanxi University. The education college of Sichuan University was abolished and changed to the education department and merged into the liberal arts college. The mathematics and physics departments of Anhui University were merged into the mathematics and physics department, and the law school was abolished. The original students were either ordered to transfer schools or changed departments. Hebei Law and Business College completely stopped recruiting students. Other schools with duplicate departments and faculties and lack of faculty and equipment and unable to develop were ordered to draft their own plans for reduction and merger and submit them to the Ministry for approval. The purpose is to completely reduce duplication and adapt to actual needs, so that the manpower and financial resources of various schools can be concentrated to engage in special enrichment and development.

2. Enriching equipment: According to statistics in the 20th year of the Republic, the new equipment expenses for colleges and universities across the country were about 6.4 million yuan, about 6.2 million yuan in the 21st year, and about 6.5 million yuan recently. It can be seen that the new equipment expenses for various schools in recent years have been about 6.4 million yuan, which cannot be said to be a considerable progress. Among the 6.4 million yuan of new equipment expenses across the country in the 20th year of the Republic, library expenses accounted for 17%, and instruments, specimens, machines, etc. accounted for 26%, totaling 43%. The remaining 57% were mostly construction, repairs, and school equipment and miscellaneous expenses. Among the 6.2 million yuan of new equipment expenses in the 21st year, library expenses accounted for 31.8%. Recently, among the 6.5 million yuan of new equipment expenses, library expenses accounted for 19%, and instruments, specimens, machines, etc. accounted for 31.8%. Recently, among the 6.5 million yuan of new equipment expenses, library expenses accounted for 18.8%, and instruments, specimens, machines, etc. accounted for 31.8%. Recently, among the 6.5 million yuan of new equipment expenses, library expenses accounted for 19%, and instruments, specimens, machines, etc. accounted for 32%. If we compare the three years, the recent library expenses have increased by about 2% compared with the 20th year, and about 0.2% compared with the 21st year. The expenses for instruments, standards, machines, etc. have increased by about 5.6% compared with the 20th year, and about 0.2% compared with the 21st year. It can be seen that various schools have indeed made considerable increases in the equipment of books and instruments. However, this increase refers to the overall situation. Individually, most of them still do not meet the statutory standards, especially private schools. According to the regulations, the equipment expenses of universities should account for at least 15% of the operating expenses, and the administrative expenses should not exceed 10%. Therefore, colleges and universities should strive to reduce administrative expenses and strive to increase equipment expenses. In addition to separately ordering various schools to seek practical enrichment of equipment such as instruments and books, the Ministry of Education has approved that equipment expenses account for 81.5% of the subsidies for private colleges and universities this year. This is the meaning of paying special attention to equipment.

Subsidies for Private Colleges and Universities are Issued Monthly 241

The Ministry of Education Formulates Payment Methods

(Nanjing, 29th) The Ministry of Education formulated the payment method for subsidies for private colleges and universities, and issued an order to private colleges and universities on the 29th to comply with it. 1. Private colleges and universities applying for subsidies that have not submitted the entire budget for this year should promptly submit the budget before receiving the subsidy. 2. All private colleges and universities that have been approved to receive subsidies should submit a detailed budget of the expenses for each subsidized item to the Ministry for approval after receiving the subsidy notification from the Ministry. For those who subsidize equipment expenses, they should also prepare a detailed list of the detailed names, uses, exact quantities, prices, and purchase locations of the items and submit it for approval. The original budget of the colleges or departments receiving subsidies shall not be reduced. 3. For those who subsidize faculty fees, the subsidized schools must submit the names, academic qualifications, salary amounts, and teaching subjects of the appointed special education teachers to the Ministry for approval before receiving the subsidy. 4. Teachers who hold special faculty positions shall not concurrently serve as teachers or positions outside the school. 5. The subsidy for special faculty fees is set at 4,000 yuan per position this year, and the minimum monthly salary shall not be less than 280 yuan. If there is a surplus in the aforementioned faculty fees, all of it shall be allocated to the equipment fees for the subject. 6. Lecture fees are limited to purchasing specialized instruments, machines, specimens, models, equipment, medicines, and books. 7. The subsidies are issued monthly by the Ministry of Education. 8. After receiving the subsidies, each school should immediately fill out the receipt and submit it. The person in charge of the college or department subsidized by the Ministry of Education should also sign and stamp it. Legal receipts must be submitted for equipment fees, and salary receipts must be submitted for education fees. The aforementioned receipts and receipts must be reported at least once every three months. 9. If the budget is not prepared or reimbursed in accordance with these methods, or if the required reports are not submitted, the subsidies may not be issued or may be suspended midway. 10. These methods shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Ministry of Education.

The Ministry of Education Orders the Issuance of Regulations for the Academic Work Advisory Office 242

(Nanjing, 29th) The Ministry of Education believes that the affairs managed by the National Academic Work Advisory Office and the educational administrative agencies of various provinces and cities should be carried out in conjunction with each other. On the 29th, the Ministry issued the regulations of the office to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities for information.

Judging Procedures for the National Elementary School Chinese Language Competition 245

The National Chinese Language Education Promotion Association founded the National Elementary School Chinese Language Competition. The Ministry of Education has issued a notice. It is said that the judging procedures of the association are divided into three types: preliminary selection, re-examination, and final selection. The judging meeting passed the procedures yesterday. Now we will explore the records below. Preliminary selection: The competition papers of public and private elementary schools in various provinces, cities, and counties across the country have been collected by the education departments and bureaus of various counties, provinces, and cities as per the order of the Ministry of Education, and the best two papers in each group will be selected before November 1, the 23rd year of the Republic, and sent to the office of the National Chinese Language Education Promotion Association at Pingle Temple, Xizang Road, Shanghai. When the association receives the papers, it will immediately issue a text to the National Elementary School Chinese Language Competition Committee of the association (hereinafter referred to as the Competition Committee). The Competition Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Competition Committee) will first register the papers, then paste the judging scoring form on the cover of the papers, and number them in groups according to the order in which they were received, and transfer them to the re-examination judging director of each group for re-examination. 2. Re-examination: The re-examination judging director of each group will receive the numbered papers and immediately meet with the judges of the group to review them in turn, evaluate the scores in various items, and record them in the judging scoring form. Then, the director of each group will summarize the scores, sign or seal them, and submit them to the Competition Committee of the association. The Competition Committee will receive the papers evaluated by the re-examination judges of each group and submit 20 papers with the highest scores in each group to the judging chairman for final selection. 3. Final selection: The judging chairman will receive the best papers from the re-examination of each group and immediately meet with the final judges to review them separately, rank them, and indicate them on the judging scoring form. The judging chairman will seal them and return them to the Competition Committee of the association, and then the Competition Committee will submit them to the association to be bound into a book and submitted to the Ministry of Education for issuing awards.

Publication of Mr. Xu Wancheng's Collection of Essays on Life Problems 253

The "Collection of Essays on Life Problems" is published by Longwen Bookstore of Dananmen in Shanghai. The author, Mr. Xu Wancheng, spent three years conducting life problem tests in major newspapers, which caused a nationwide sensation. A large number of young people responded enthusiastically. He also conducted tests on the three major problems of young people—education, career choice, and love—in this newspaper, collecting public opinions and compiling them into a book. Mr. Xu is truly the first to do so. The entire book is divided into three parts—upper, middle, and lower—with nearly 300,000 words. The upper part consists of Mr. Xu's own works, with key sections including: 1. What is the ultimate meaning of life? 2. Advice to young people seeking education. 3. Advice to young people choosing careers and serving society. 4. Advice to young people in love and getting married. 5. How to cultivate a happy life and build a rational family life. 6. How should young people strive to create? 7. How should young people transform society and the nation? 8. Where should I stand regarding modern trends and ideologies? 9. How should I deal with the current social situation? etc. The middle part contains statistical answers from life problem surveys in major newspapers. The lower part includes over sixty essays and an article titled "My View of Life," featuring the personal life philosophies of more than twenty celebrities, with practical viewpoints. It is said that every purchase of the collection comes with complimentary inscriptions from scholars encouraging young people, including inscriptions from Cai Yuanpei, Jiang Menglin, Ma Junwu, Li Shicen, and over forty others, compiled and printed like diplomas, serving as mottoes. Each volume is priced at two yuan, with a 40% discount for respondents using coupons, exclusively available at the distribution center of Longwen Bookstore of Dananmen in Shanghai.

Joint Conference of Shanghai Universities Resolves to Strictly Prohibit Students from Entering Dance Halls 256

And Requests the Ministry of Education to Revise Military Training Regulations

The Joint Conference of Shanghai Universities held an executive committee meeting at the YMCA on Eight Immortals Bridge on the 27th at noon. Zhang Yong of Guanghua University, Qiu Weiyu of Jiaotong University, Liu Zansi of Hujiang University, Shen Pengfei of Jinan University, Ou Yuanhuai of Daxia University, and Jin Tongyin of Fudan University, among others, attended and resolved two important matters: 1. The Director-General of Training and the Ministry of Education have stipulated that centralized training will be implemented for military training in high schools and above from the 24th academic year. However, the stipulated training time interferes with the regular curriculum of each school. Chu Minyi and Liu Zanen were jointly elected to submit a written statement to the Ministry of Education to seek revisions. 2. Strictly Prohibit Students from Entering Dance Halls: A resolution was passed to cooperate with the Municipal Government to jointly investigate and prohibit such activities, and offenders will be severely punished.
