Free Talk

Words and Actions 272

— Zhou Muzhai

One who is sick and refuses medicine often meets a mediocre doctor. Those with average talent often meet mediocre people. Those who are known to be talented, if they do not do good, will do evil, and will never be content to live a mediocre life. Doing good is mostly for others, while doing evil is only for oneself. Those with talent would rather do evil. The more talent one has, the more capable one is of doing evil. Those who are good at it show only the good and conceal the evil. Evil is embellished by good. That is why Laozi and Zhuangzi advocated the elimination of sagehood and knowledge.

However, Laozi and Zhuangzi were also extremely intelligent people. A Dao De Jing, a Zhuangzi, reveal the secrets of the human world, and are extremely thorough. In theory, evil should be reduced. But from another point of view, it is no different from teaching a monkey to climb a tree, which cannot reduce evil, but instead encourages it. This may be the bitter truth they wanted to say but did not. If words were converted into actions, they could become the greatest treachery.

Like these two, they are living examples, like understanding the principle of cloth curtains, yet also covering themselves with a layer of cloth curtain. Clever people will say, "Today's me is not yesterday's me," flipping their tongues and transforming themselves. In fact, they are also tearing off the cloth curtain and replacing it with another layer, or simply revealing their true form.

Wushan 273

— Yin Guang

In the twilight of dusk, the boat slowly anchored at Wushan. The passengers had already strolled onto the deck, some holding pipes, some yawning, some paying attention to the tea attendants' instructions, and all gazing curiously at the side of the riverbank where the castle was located, as if they could find some eye-catching architecture and lively markets.

However, all that met their eyes was a glaring desolation.

The city squatted on top of a not-very-tall earthen hill, low and pitiful. It seemed that it was deliberately squatting high, not to show the characteristics of a mountain city, but to allow people to appreciate its decay and backwardness. That is to say, in the continuous turmoil and under poor natural conditions, a town that is based on an important river line is how it is on the verge of extinction.

The observers shook their heads and already showed a disappointed expression. They didn't seem to feel any interest at all. A young man who looked like he was out for the first time stared wide-eyed and muttered to himself:

Oh, so that's it? He even gave a bitter laugh from his nose.

Many people returned to their berths. From the turbid river, three or four gray-brown boats were lazily floating over. But there was neither the clamor of selling food nor the call of soliciting customers. It seemed that the purpose of those boat owners was just to rush over to share a bit of the so-called excitement of the world. However, because of this sporadic embellishment, the river seemed even more desolate.

Is anyone going ashore? People who stayed on the deck asked each other with boredom.

Come to the back, come to the back. The small boat then rowed harder towards the stern of the steamboat.

Don't delay, or you'll cause trouble! The boat soldiers urged each of the passengers going ashore.

When I, together with a tea attendant and two small-time opium merchants, were in a dilapidated boat, the night was gradually deepening. A kind of eerie feeling surrounded us. But, although the place where we were moored was still in the middle of this long gorge, the eeriness was the desolation of Guanghan, and did not carry the deepness and solemnity that should be in the mountain gorge. Because the mountain range rushing down from the upper reaches seemed to suddenly collapse here, leaving only some earthen hills and small mountains, and a stretch of rocky riverbank.

Hey, Fangfang pointed the empty wine bottle on the boat and shouted, you should also spend some money to repair it.

Easy to say, repair it...

As if strangely blaming the accuser for not knowing the situation, the boatman did not finish his sentence, then lazily turned his head and took care of his own oars.

This was an old man in his fifties, with a sandy white beard and a dark, wrinkled face. He lazily wielded his old oars inlaid with new wood, his waist stretching and bending, half-closed eyes, as if his work was not for food, but to pass the time he had already lived through. Due to the tea attendant's urgent urging, the boat was soon anchored.

Old man, I asked the boatman, who now only needed to take care of the direction of the boat, I heard that the bandit has come again?

Yes, it's happening again. The army just left a few days ago.

Then the two opium merchants shifted their bodies and began to show off their knowledge. In such a conversation, the boat sailed to the shore. So, walking across a sandy beach mixed with gravel and walking up the sloping path, we entered that desolate county town.

However, speaking of the county town, its size and liveliness were actually not comparable to the market towns in other areas. Moreover, it still maintained the old appearance of all the small towns in the past: narrow streets, low houses, and bamboo poles for drying clothes and firewood to be split across the streets. A little boy, with one hand holding up his pants and one hand holding a rattan whip-like tow rope, cried out and ran towards several frantically running piglets.

On the steps of several teahouses, there were stoves and equipment for cooking opium. The two opium merchants went to discuss their business seriously, and the tea attendant disappeared under the eaves of a dark cave. And I, who was already very depressed at that time, wandered alone in the market until I gathered my companions, the opium merchant and the tea attendant, at the gate of the city.

We stepped on the steep return path again, but I was still oppressed by a kind of restless mood.

Mr. Zhang, look up! The tea attendant suddenly greeted me with a laughing tone, while opening his electric torch.

Following the direction of the light, I looked up at the top of the electric pole on the side of the road: there hung three terrible things that had already lost their color of blood. But I did not panic as my companions had hoped. After staring for a while, I returned to my own thoughts.

When the boat was approaching the steamboat, we encountered trouble from the ship-guarding soldiers.

This was in the autumn of 1931. Early the next morning, the boat entered the Wuxia Gorge with cliffs on both sides.

An Honest and Sincere Man 274

— Bi Bing

Luo Fu is an honest and sincere person; at least, he is confident in this about himself. Although Luo Fu has lived in Shanghai for eight or nine years, and although, besides Shanghai, Luo Fu has also traveled to Hong Kong, Macau, Tianjin, Beiping, Hankou, Qingdao, Jinan, Nanjing, Jiujiang, and other commercial ports within the Chinese territory, and although Luo Fu has experienced many different kinds of occupations, such as teacher, contributor, political work in the military, railway inspector, and the like, and Luo Fu has also experienced various different ways of life, such as renting a room for twelve or thirteen yuan, and being so poor as to have nowhere to stand, yet, it may be hard to believe, Luo Fu can still be said to be an honest and sincere person to this day.

Luo Fu considers himself to have a very deep understanding of worldly wisdom and human relationships, and he believes that he can clearly judge good and evil, wisdom and foolishness, regardless of the length of time he interacts with people. However, many people think that Luo Fu does not understand worldly wisdom and human relationships and treat him as someone easy to deceive. And Luo Fu has indeed been deceived and played with, once, twice, three times… to increase his experiences.

This person is hopeless; he will always be a wandering pauper. He doesn't even know the basic rules of life. Many people, after deceiving and playing with Luo Fu, turn around and blame him in a seemingly well-intentioned way.

………………

Luo Fu could not say half a word in rebuttal after being blamed, because the current society... especially Shanghai or other cities, simply does not need honest and sincere people. Honest and sincere people simply cannot stand a foothold in this kind of society. After being blamed, Luo Fu, of course, could not refute others, except to endure it and complain to himself.

Sometimes, because the wounds given by being played with and deceived were too deep, and the lessons too many, Luo Fu also wanted to buck up a bit, to be a person... a modern person, of course, a person who adapts to modern society, a person who can tell lies and deceive. In that way, perhaps he could also stand a foothold in this society.

Hey! Are you going to Guangdong today?

No! I'm going to Hankou tomorrow.

I heard you've been very close to Mr. Huang recently. I think you'll be successful in the near future.

I don't know Mr. Huang. This person is very good at using tricks. You must not fall for his tricks.

Such knowingly false answers, others might think that Luo Fu is really good at dealing with people, able to tell hypocritical and deceptive words. Therefore, they also secretly express admiration for Luo Fu, thinking that this child is teachable. However, only God believes that when Luo Fu deliberately says these knowingly false answers because of deep stimulation, Luo Fu's inner pain is unbearable, and it exceeds the severe trauma caused by treating people with loyalty and sincerity, only to be played with by others with hypocritical and deceptive means by several times, because this is not only deceiving others, but perhaps also deceiving himself. Why do I have to be hypocritical and deceptive in what I do and what I say to people! Thinking like this, Luo Fu might cry and kneel in front of the person who heard Luo Fu's hypocritical and deceptive words, begging him to forgive him.

What's going on, is he crazy!

However, others are, after all, others. When others hear Luo Fu's hypocritical and deceptive words, they may not even realize that they are not true and think that he is truly treating people with loyalty and sincerity, or they may realize that they are false words, and admire Luo Fu's shrewdness in dealing with people. But now, waiting for Luo Fu to tell the truth, and frankly self-report, repent, but instead despise him and think that Luo Fu's behavior is inhuman. As a result, Luo Fu's sincere repentance is despised by others.

This person is really hopeless; he might as well commit suicide.

Although no one said so to his face, some people advocated this behind his back. Later, when they met Luo Fu, they would show contempt or keep a respectful distance.

Therefore, Luo Fu's experience in worldly wisdom and human relationships, although rich, is ultimately useless. If he tries to apply it, he will only mess things up and damage his reputation as an honest and sincere man. This reason makes Luo Fu afraid to tell even half a lie when dealing with people in the future, and even if he accidentally says a word or two wrong, he must quickly correct it, lest others think he is playing tricks.

An honest and sincere man increasingly lives up to his name.

Therefore, Luo Fu's only friends are children or young people who are just beginning to understand the world, because these people, like Luo Fu, treat people with honesty and sincerity. Birds of a feather flock together, and they can understand each other. However, when those children or young people grow up and understand the world, they will also treat people with hypocrisy and deception. Then, Luo Fu will be played with, deceived, and despised by those children or young people. Luo Fu will become estranged from these young gentlemen whom he once regarded as children and young people. Then, he will associate with a new group of children and young people. But when the future comes, and those second batch (?) of children and young people become young gentlemen and understand worldly wisdom and human relationships, Luo Fu will only be able to associate with the third batch (?) of children and young people. Such a formula, a revolving door of replacements, has been going on for eight or nine years now. During these years, the fifth batch (?) of children and young people have become young gentlemen in today's society, but Luo Fu still does not improve. Luo Fu is now only associating with the sixth batch of children and young people.

Luo Fu will never be able to gain any experience in the most important lesson in life and society! He will carry this nickname given to honest and sincere people until the end of his life.

Streets of Nanyang (1) 275

— Hei Ying

Smoothly, solidly, paved with a layer of asphalt. No trees on either side, no tall, magnificent buildings. All are two- or three-story buildings, and not very tidy: some are old, some are modern buildings. But you can probably know that the Chinese will always love to do their business in old shops.

Those facing east put up the white canvas awnings before the sun rises, to prevent the tropical sun from baking them an hour later. On the canvas, the shop name is painted in two or even three languages: you can imagine how different Chinese characters and Latin letters are when put together.

Gradually, there are more and more people on the street, and more and more cars. The people are extremely mixed: if you stand in the center of the road where the Malay police station stands and watch for twenty or thirty minutes, you will see the following different kinds of humans displayed in front of you:

Yellow-faced Chinese and Japanese. Blue-eyed Germans, Dutch, British, Portuguese, Americans…. Black Africans, Kling people…. (You won't be able to tell them apart without some knowledge of ethnology.)

In the cars, sit the descendants of those who became rich from rubber plantations during the European War: when they think back to those good old days, they all shake their heads and sigh. Horse-drawn carriages seem to be a special existence here, arousing the curiosity of some newcomers, who stare unblinkingly at the horses galloping forward and the coachmen. Bicycles come and go in droves: sometimes you see young women riding them. Their skill and naturalness in driving must be surprising to everyone, right?

Elementary school students carrying schoolbags walk to school, piling on smiling faces, rushing forward with a whoosh. If you are walking in front of them, they will catch up with you in a moment.

Children growing up in Nanyang are always lively and adorable. An active, assertive personality makes them have to fight once a day. You may be surprised to go to the Malay police: why don't they interfere when they see children fighting? But, wait ten minutes, and the loser will follow the others meekly on their way.

The small carts of the Kling people selling ice cream and lemonade also appear on the street, the bells ringing ding-ding. Some people, regardless of whether they are thirsty or not, drop three or five copper coins and have a cup of sweet ice water to drink. The Kling people, with a face full of beards, slowly push the gauze-covered carts and turn the corner.

Square Calligraphy (5) 276

— Wei He

Seeing me hesitating and unable to choose, he helped me flip through it again and again for half a day. Then, without even drying the inkstone, without even taking off his boots, he helped me grind the ink, cut the paper, because he was afraid of cutting the paper wrong, he measured it again and again carefully, folded it again and again, and after the paper was cut, he used his fingers to draw fingerprints on it, and used his mother's face powder to draw crosses on it, constantly saying:

You have to write evenly and neatly, arrange the positions well, especially the couplets must be written in a straight line, and be careful not to write them upside down, crooked…

A solemn light appeared on his face, his wrinkled skin tightening and loosening, constantly changing shape, his lips also seemed to be distorted by the stimulation of excessive excitement. While using his skinny hands to tightly clamp the new ink that he had specially fetched, he glanced with his two rat-like eyes at the encyclopedia wrapped in a black cover, his mouth opening and closing, as if he was chanting in a low voice.

I also bought a new sheep hair brush, a real square calligraphy brush, all for Uncle Zhang's sake!

Everything was arranged properly. Afterwards, like opening some kind of exhibition, my father went to invite several gentlemen from the neighborhood to watch me write. These people were all first-class characters in the village, running scams and doing all kinds of evil. They didn't do any real work all year round, but they were all dressed up and ate well, not only despicable and vulgar, but also arrogant to the extreme. I have always looked down on these parasites, but my father invited them to watch me write calligraphy, like proctors, so my aversion to them increased even more.

I heard these parasites, who seemed to know everything and had no shame, praising me incessantly:

Congratulations, congratulations, you have such a son, you are truly blessed!

Several others, unable to hide their feelings, said in envious and jealous tones:

It's all about face! Uncle Zhang's face, what else is there to say?

Commercial News

Bullion Rises, Silver Falls, Standard Gold Continues to Rise by $1.20 277

Market Conditions Unstable, Recorded at Around 80 Yuan

The gold market yesterday saw a rise in bullion due to shrinking overseas silver markets and exchange rates. Public sentiment remained stable, and as unfavorable news had not been confirmed by newspapers, buyers were still active and prices rose. However, the future showed signs of change, with many potential headwinds. In the early morning, overseas silver markets shrank in both the UK and the US, and the forward price of silver in Monte Carlo also decreased. The price of spot gold in London rose by two pence, and exchange rates also fell, causing slight anxiety. Off-market pre-market trading opened and immediately rose to $83.40. The central bank's official rates were announced, with the UK and the US unchanged, and the customs gold unit rising by 3 li. The forbidden gold standard price was set at $992.50, opening at a high. Unfortunately, major players took advantage of the high prices to sell aggressively, and banks were also hesitant, gradually falling back within the $80 mark. However, as Chinese merchants continued to buy, and the HSBC official rates were announced, with the UK unchanged and the US shrinking by 0.0625, the exchange rate was able to recover slightly, and the price of gold gradually rose again. However, the rising trend was difficult to sustain, and selling pressure remained latent, with sellers becoming active again, and prices falling back within the $80 mark. The domestic market also hardened accordingly. At this time, the situation suddenly weakened, but the overall trend was not downward, and buyers appeared when prices were low, gradually rising back above the $80 mark. At noon, the situation was quite stable. The afternoon market opened steadily, but public sentiment was clearly bullish, and major players had a renewed appetite for buying. The supply side lacked momentum, and short positions also started to panic, rising at one point. However, banks continued to supply, and sellers became active again after that. However, as Indian silver prices were reported to be shrinking by five annas, the market remained hesitant. Yesterday, 2,000 boxes of 90-pound double-jointed Italian tinplate were ordered at a price of 35 shillings 4 pence per box, an increase of 2 pence compared to last Saturday's telegram. According to news from foreign firms, the overseas market is exceptionally good, and there is probably no hope of a price decrease in the near future.

A telegram from New York said that 200-pound steel from the company was priced at 8 gold yuan per box, slightly lower than before, but local firms were unable to calculate a profit and there were still no orders.

申報 本埠增刊

Shanghai Shen Bao Local Supplement

談言

Essays

冤哉，我們的大豆 301

A Tragedy, Our Soybeans

— ＨＹ

— HY

東三省的特產，首屆一指的要算是大豆了。

The specialty of the Three Eastern Provinces, the most prominent, would have to be soybeans.

隨著東北被佔，大豆也淪入日本帝國主義產業部門之內。這也算不了什麼，十地，人民已都屬了人家，自然無法收回這類特產。

With the Northeast occupied, soybeans also fell into the industrial sector of Japanese imperialism. This isn't a big deal. The land and the people belong to someone else, so naturally there's no way to recover these kinds of specialties.

不過，近日報載日德締結秘密恊定，而這恊定的內容，據哈瓦斯社倫敦電訊，說是由日本每年供給德國一百萬噸大豆，用以交換德國的化學品，炸藥，機關槍，飛機等項殺人武器。這實在是值得我們注意的。

However, recently it was reported that Japan and Germany had concluded a secret agreement. According to a Reuters dispatch from London, the content of this agreement is that Japan will supply Germany with one million tons of soybeans annually, in exchange for German chemicals, explosives, machine guns, airplanes, and other weapons of murder. This is really something that we should pay attention to.

日本和德國這項恊定，不論這通電訊的播發，是出於德國的對頭冤家法國的通訊社，也許這是別有作用，但我們可以拋除這一點不談，單談恊定的成立，我們認爲確有可能。何況，如果用我們一句舊話無風不起浪來說，這電訊總還有幾分是可靠的。

Regarding this agreement between Japan and Germany, regardless of whether this telegram was broadcast by the French news agency, Germany's nemesis, and perhaps this has another purpose, we can put this aside and just talk about the establishment of the agreement. We believe that it is entirely possible. Besides, if we use an old saying, "no wind, no waves," then this telegram must have some reliability.

關於恊定完成後的重要性，筆者不願多說，讓我們的國際政治專家去寫些評論罷，筆者在這里要說的話，是爲我們的特產喊一聲冤。

Regarding the importance of the completion of the agreement, I don't want to say too much. Let our international political experts write some comments. What I want to say here is to cry out a wrong for our special product.

如其我們的東北不失掉，我們不是也可以用大豆和德國（或是別國）換些武器麼？固然，我們不贊成殺人，要反對戰爭的，但是最低限度總可以用到自衛上。請問日本從什麼地方得來的大豆，是他國里的特產品？不是的，就是用了我們東北民衆血汁耕種出來的大豆！這是毫無疑義的。

If our Northeast hadn't been lost, couldn't we also use soybeans to exchange for weapons with Germany (or another country)? Of course, we don't approve of murder and want to oppose war, but at the very least, we can use them for self-defense. May I ask, where did Japan get the soybeans? Are they a specialty of his country? No, they are the soybeans cultivated with the blood and sweat of our Northeastern people! There is no doubt about this.

還記得近兩年來，東北農產品的狂跌，跌得銷路全無。一般農民只有把產品存在家里藏著。大豆是東北農產品中主要部門，農民受害更甚。我們試問這是受到什麼影響？就是受了日本帝國主義有計劃的迫害。現在，我們可以替東北農民道一聲喜，爲的存藏每家的大豆可以賣出，但是日本帝國主義在這種情形下的低價收買，當真發了一筆大財。

Remember the sharp drop in agricultural products in the Northeast over the past two years, so sharp that there were no sales at all. Ordinary farmers could only store the products at home. Soybeans are a major sector of agricultural products in the Northeast, and farmers suffered even more. May we ask, what was the impact? It was the planned persecution by Japanese imperialism. Now, we can congratulate the farmers in the Northeast because the soybeans stored in each household can be sold, but Japanese imperialism really made a fortune by buying them at low prices in this situation.

說來說去吃虧的總是我們自已。人家用我們的東西，換得來武器，將來還要來殺戮我們，這是多麼說不出口的事情！

In the end, we are always the ones who suffer. People use our things to exchange for weapons, and they will come to kill us in the future. How unspeakable this is!

所以，筆者因此要們的大豆喊一聲冤：冤哉，我們的大豆。

Therefore, I want to cry out a wrong for our soybeans: a tragedy, our soybeans.

回憶 302

Reminiscence

— 蕙人

— Hui Ren

在你感到身處寂寞或無聊的當兒，例如在秋風蕭瑟，淫雨紛飛，或者秋夜望著明月，聽著秋蟲悲鳴，獨自烯著枝捲煙，靜坐在室內清閑的時候，有意識的或無意識的會翻出些藏在深處的回憶。

When you feel lonely or bored, such as when the autumn wind is bleak, the rain is incessant, or on an autumn night, looking at the bright moon, listening to the mournful chirping of autumn insects, smoking a cigarette alone, sitting quietly indoors in leisure, you will consciously or unconsciously recall some memories hidden deep within.

不論是歡樂的或悲哀的，總會刺激著頭腦，使你感覺到這一回憶的來到，是多少的帶來了一些苦悶：像趙景深先生在人間世第九期上也用著傷威的筆調這樣地寫著：不可復回的過去呵，我寂寞，我要燒掉我的書和我的書桌，我要擲去我的筆……

Whether joyful or sad, they always stimulate the mind, making you feel that the arrival of this memory brings some depression: like Mr. Zhao Jingshen writing in the ninth issue of Renjian Shi with a mournful tone: "Irrecoverable past, I am lonely, I want to burn my books and my desk, I want to throw away my pen…"

所謂苦悶之嘆者，在文人的眼里具體點說就是牢騷。

The so-called sigh of depression, in the eyes of the literati, is specifically grumbling.

在這牢騷中所勾引出來的，雖有著使人不堪回首的印象，或者平淡得簡直沒有回憶之價值，但這沒有價值的回憶到了現在卻也有其特殊的風味，像每一個事實的過去在自已生命史上，佔了值得光榮的一頁。

Although what is evoked in this grumbling has an impression that makes people unbearable to look back on, or it is so plain that it has no value of memory, this valueless memory now has its own special flavor, like every fact of the past occupies a glorious page in one's own life history.

就以一個人來說，在青年時，感覺到兒童時代的生活比現在要好得許多—但是或許在兒童時代也並未感覺到有什麼滿足的地方—但這些早已在腦間消失，所意識到的全是些兒童時的天真可愛，於是在青年時代，天真的搜索便成了一個回憶的題材：假使在老年時代，那麼青年時代又成爲了回憶了對象：假使至將要入木時，那麼連老年時候的一刻靜穆生活也覺得有留戀。

Taking a person as an example, in youth, one feels that childhood life was much better than now—but perhaps in childhood one did not feel anything satisfying—but these have long disappeared from the mind, and what is realized are all the innocence and loveliness of childhood. Thus, in youth, the search for innocence becomes a theme of reminiscence: if in old age, then youth becomes the object of reminiscence: if one is about to die, then even a moment of quiet life in old age feels nostalgic.

因爲身子一靜下來的時候，腦子就回到回溯里，所以對於自已所處身的現在很少機會去體騐它：但奇怪的，就是不去注意的現在會在將來又成爲值得去思戀的一段。

Because when the body calms down, the mind returns to retrospection, so there is little opportunity to experience the present in which one finds oneself: but strangely, the present that is not paid attention to will become a period worthy of nostalgia in the future.

對於現實的不滿，是由於過去回憶奪所呈現出來的而對照著來的，但到底是怎樣的不滿，卻沒有加以具體的體騐，祗不過感覺到過去是有點可愛，而現在是苦悶，痛苦的，不問從前是怎樣的可愛，現在又是怎樣的痛苦。

Dissatisfaction with reality comes from the contrast presented by past memories, but what kind of dissatisfaction it is, has not been concretely experienced, only that the past is somewhat lovely, and the present is depressed, painful, without asking how lovely the past was, and how painful the present is.

所以有人說：人是盲目的愛著，盲目的恨著。但是盲目的愛恨民消費了不少的時間。

Therefore, some people say: people love blindly, and hate blindly. But blind love and hate consume a lot of time.

週年 303

Anniversary

— 夢瀾

— Meng Lan

媽臨終時的那種痛苦掙扎的情狀，還透新鮮的印在我腦膜上，像昨天的事似的，不，像上一個鐘頭里的事似的。

The scene of Mom's painful struggle at the time of her death is still freshly imprinted on my mind, like it was yesterday, no, like it was an hour ago.

可是，現在是整整的一年啦。

But, now it's been a whole year.

一年啦，那太快的光陰呵！

A year, such a quick passage of time!

媽在生前，我對她是沒有好感的，直到臨終一面擬著電報告訴姊姊的時候，還是像替別人家寫便條擬的，滑有一些感想，更沒有所謂悲哀。

When Mom was alive, I didn't have good feelings towards her, until I was drafting the telegram to tell my sister at the time of her death, it was still like drafting a memo for someone else, with only a few slippery thoughts, and even less so-called sorrow.

那沒有好感的理由，大概是因爲母親過度的愛護，以致變成了過度的嘮叨，於是在任性的倔強的孩子的心中，便成爲討厭了。

The reason for not having good feelings was probably because my mother's excessive love turned into excessive nagging, and in the heart of a willful, stubborn child, it became annoying.

譬如少穿了一件衣服，便會說上一個鐘頭，而我是會把善意視作敵意的，以爲這麼大了，還老是嚕蘇著吃穿。

For example, if I wore one less piece of clothing, she would talk about it for an hour, and I would see kindness as hostility, thinking that I'm so old, and she's still always nagging about what to eat and wear.

次數一多，便不問理由的聽見母親嘮叨，便一溜煙的走開。

After it happened so many times, I wouldn't even ask the reason and just take off in a puff of smoke when I heard my mother nagging.

這樣，是重重的傷了慈母的心。

In this way, I severely hurt my loving mother's heart.

此外，便是新舊思想的衡突，而我又是不懂小節的：在舊一代的人以爲應該盡禮的地方，我往往一笑視之。

In addition, there was the conflict between new and old ideas, and I didn't understand the minor details: in places where the older generation thought I should pay my respects, I often laughed it off.

記得有一次，—那是母親抱恨終身的一次呵，我深深的紀錄，—從鄉間回來，回爲舟車上過度的勞頓，到家又天還不曾亮，於是便沒有母親房里去請安，便回到自已房里睡了，可是，這自已不經意的過失，在媽的心目中，是以爲掉了娘了，使她整整不樂了好幾天，直到病重的時候，還不時的把這件事提起。

I remember one time—it was the one that Mother regretted for the rest of her life, I deeply record it—coming back from the countryside, because of the excessive fatigue from the boat and car, and it wasn't even dawn when I got home, so I didn't go to my mother's room to pay my respects, but went back to my own room to sleep. But, this unintentional mistake of mine, in Mom's eyes, was like she lost her daughter, making her unhappy for several days, until she was seriously ill, she would still bring up this matter from time to time.

當時，倔強的任性的我以爲媽不該這樣的求全責備，心里也感到幾分不快，可是，又誰料這小小的事件居然使媽抱恨終身的呢？

At the time, the stubborn and willful me thought that Mom shouldn't be so demanding, and I felt a bit unhappy in my heart, but who would have thought that this small incident would actually make Mom regret it for the rest of her life?

到現在，還有誰肯嘮叨的地牽住了手問冷問暖？

Now, who is willing to nag and hold my hand, asking if I'm cold or warm?

還有誰怪我祗吃了一碗飯便放下了筷呢？

Who else blames me for putting down my chopsticks after eating only one bowl of rice?

人家的悲哀是會眼著時日消失去了的，而我，跟了時日的增長，增長了我的悲思。

Other people's sorrows will disappear with the passage of time, but for me, with the growth of time, my sadness grows.

媽在時，家庭里是有種說不出的融洽的樂趣的，而現在，媽死了剛一年，家庭的融洽的空氣在那里？

When Mom was alive, there was an unspeakable harmonious joy in the family, but now, Mom has been dead for just a year, where is the harmonious atmosphere of the family?

這倔強的任性的孩子，又爲了忍不住種種刺激，做了家庭的叛徒，到社會來困苦地和社會搏門了，媽，要是你在世的話，你肯允許你的孩子過著這樣艱難的生活嗎？

This stubborn and willful child, unable to resist the various stimuli, has become a traitor to the family, and has come to society to struggle painfully with society, Mom, if you were alive, would you allow your child to live such a difficult life?

媽，要是你有靈的話，在這週年祭里，你看一看現在家庭里的景象，你一家要放心痛哭的呢？

Mom, if you have a soul, in this anniversary, if you look at the current scene in the family, your whole family must cry with pain, right?

可是，現在是，再見不到媽清瘦的臉上流著凄苦的淚了。

But, now, I can no longer

Minor Ailment in Late Autumn 304

— A'er

Some literati say: three parts illness, seven parts leisure, a minor ailment has its own unique charm. However, as for me? Whenever I feel unwell, I always feel extremely troubled. I can neither write articles nor do other work. I am just restless all day and night. So I am a bit doubtful about these experienced talks of the literati. However, who has the leisure to care about these things amidst the anxieties of life? But I finally collapsed and got what is called sick. I was already worried when I wasn't sick, so what now that I'm sick? What am I going to do? It was already difficult to cope when I wasn't sick, if I really get sick, then there's even less I can do. I fully experienced the autumn wind blowing and catching a cold! I developed a slight fever and chills. I fell onto the bed in a daze. At this time, in the cold and quiet garret room, besides my own moans, I couldn't hear any other sound. Not only was there not seven parts leisure, but there was twelve hundred thousand parts distress. The pain of the illness itself could be tolerated. However, who is going to struggle and bear the burden of life? Don't say that when you are sick you can't get up and find food to eat, and you can't even eat, and that someone and money are needed to serve you, to make milk and get water for you to drink. Just the oppression of life is enough to make the illness worse. Even if it gradually gets better without medical treatment, there are still no seven parts leisure, only increased worries in my heart! How to deal with rent, food expenses, and a weak body? The three parts illness are gone, so my mood should be better! In fact, it's getting worse and worse, and I'm even more worried about food, clothing, and shelter! I force myself to write articles, hoping to exchange some manuscript fees for relief, which can temporarily replace the seven parts leisure! However, my hands are weak and my head is dizzy and unclear. If I think about it, my head hurts even more, so I can only secretly wonder what to do? And fall back on the bed. The bed no longer brings any leisure. Even though I try my best to avoid distress. So-called good rest, don't think too much. But how can this be avoided? This requires certain conditions to be able to rest and avoid it. Otherwise, you need to have the ability to not need food, clothing, and shelter. Or have some savings of your own. Therefore, the so-called three parts illness, seven parts leisure is not something that ordinary people can achieve!

East, West, South, North 305

— San Duo

Amidst the talk of economic downturn, shops are adopting the strategy of using huge advertisements to attract customers, which is said to be quite effective. And radio advertisements are even more unexpectedly effective.

A certain shop specializing in selling aviation lottery tickets reported: ... Our shop has repeatedly won huge prizes. The eighth lottery draw is not far away. Please come to our shop. All kinds of numbers are available for you to choose from.

This advertisement can be said to be extremely authentic. It first introduced itself, explaining its winning achievements from the first to the seventh lottery draws. Although there is no case to verify, Shanghai people are accustomed to using their ears instead of their eyes, so advertising effectiveness has naturally occurred. Secondly, it reported that the draw is not far away, which is even more clever. It is like saying that money is flying past your door, hurry up and grab it! You must grab it! Of course, come to our shop. At this point, the advertisement has been successfully completed. According to the reporter's understanding, because business has already been attracted. However, it insisted on saying that the numbers are complete, which seems to be somewhat self-defeating. Imagine, among the 500,000 numbers, if there are no more huge prizes won repeatedly, would there still be gambling friends who listen to your advertisement?

The Violin is Silent 306

— Wu Fei

The violin is silent! Really, it has been at least a week since I heard this melodious, nostalgic violin sound!

A week ago, when I carried a book and walked to the park every morning, I had to pass through a shallow alley and a winding short path. In a small Western-style house at the end of this lane, there was always a section by section, sound by sound of melodious violin music sent out, rippling in the dim morning light. Although I had to pass there at 5:30, it seemed that the violin sound was even earlier than me. So when I routinely walked near that small Western-style house at the end of the alley every day, I would hear the clanging melody floating out from this small Western-style house, slowly floating out.

I don't know why, but I always loved listening to this sound. Therefore, whenever I passed there, I had to linger in front of that small Western-style house for a while before reluctantly leaving. Sometimes the violin music didn't end, and I didn't even want to leave, preferring not to go to the park and not wanting to read a book. Really, this melody was too inviting! So full of resentment and longing, so like weeping and complaining.

Although the small Western-style house was not very large or very high, it was quite exquisite. It was built along the riverbank. One side was the river, and the other side was a garden. The air was extremely good, and the scenery was also excellent. People who live here must be very fortunate. But from whose fingers did that melodious violin sound come from? Was it the male owner? No, judging from the graceful melody, it must be a female owner, maybe a young lady, definitely, definitely.

In order to dispel this curious doubt, I paid attention to which window the melody was coming from every day.

One day, I got up at 5:30 as usual, and also carried a book as usual and walked on the road to the park. When I walked to the front of that small Western-style house, the melodious, sorrowful sound waves were rippling around again, and there was also a nightingale-like singing voice, which was clearly a young lady's singing voice. So I leaned on the iron railing by the riverbank and looked up, looked up, and the miracle that had been pressing on my heart for a long time was finally discovered by me: the beautiful young lady's shadow had already been captured in my eyes.

Isn't it so? That was a young lady, a beautiful young lady. I thought in surprise like this.

She was wearing a honey-colored thin silk morning gown, with soft, white feathers attached to the collar and cuffs. The slightly curled hair moved slightly. The golden sunlight shone on her face, making her even more charming. Whose young lady is this! I couldn't help but stare at her foolishly.

From then on, a corner of my empty mind was filled with this innocent and lively young lady's jade figure. So every morning, more important than any homework, I had to admire her beautiful appearance once and listen to the violin sound.

For several months like this, I had never been disappointed once. However, there were also two times that disappointed me. One time was three days, and the other time was one day. It turned out that she went to Hangzhou for three days, and she had a headache for one day, so she didn't come to play. But I blessed her, at all times.

But things were too unfortunate! She finally died of diphtheria in the xx hospital this autumn - that is, a week ago! From then on, where is the beauty, the violin sound will never be heard again!

The owner of the violin is dead! The violin is silent! Now, when I walk here every day, I always shout like that in a low voice, but it finally makes me feel as if I have lost a heart, and I am now offering my deepest condolences to her spirit!

Shen Bao Architectural Weekly

A Glimpse of Architectural Investment in the Shanghai Concessions in the Past Ten Years 312

— Pillow Wood

If we try to tour the Shanghai Public Concession and the French Concession for a week, we will be shocked and sigh endlessly at the various buildings scattered throughout them. After all, what are the achievements of the buildings in the two concessions? Last week, the Mainland Daily revealed the number of buildings in the British and French concessions in the past ten years, which is listed and translated as follows:

Among them, the amount of construction in 1930 was the highest, with 8,836 buildings built in the Public Concession alone, worth a total of 65 million yuan. This was when the National Army established Nanjing, the situation was peaceful, and there was hope for prosperity. Later, in 1932, due to the January 28th Shanghai War, the construction industry also declined sharply, with the amount of investment only reaching more than 25 million, less than half of that in 1930. However, the French Concession suffered less from the Shanghai War, so the degree of decline was only about one-third. This can be clearly seen from the table above. But how long ago was it, and the total amount of architectural investment in this year has shown a rapid rise and vigorous increase. As of September of this year, the total amount of the Public Concession and the French Concession has reached more than 41 million yuan, which is actually alarming. Let's try to list the total amount of assets and construction categories of the Public Concession last year as follows to observe the trend of construction in this city. The total amount of construction assets in the Public Concession in 1933 was 35,463,740 yuan, with more than 5,130 buildings, including 3,545 ordinary Chinese houses, 257 Western-style houses, 13 apartments, 13 office buildings, 204 shops, 4 theaters, 7 schools, 27 factories, 63 industrial buildings, 20 storage yards, 98 warehouses, and 879 other buildings. The distribution of all buildings in the French Concession and the two districts this year is also roughly similar.

The reason why Shanghai's construction industry can develop so well is that the Shanghai Chinese and foreign banks, trust companies, and insurance companies have absorbed all the national funds from the countryside, which has been increasing day by day. Those who hold this huge amount of money, in view of the instability of public bonds, standard gold, and cloth transactions, have no other way but to invest in real estate construction. Therefore, the development of Shanghai's construction industry is an inevitable trend in the bankruptcy of the rural economy and the畸形development of the city. Moreover, due to the high price of land, there is a natural reason for the increasing height of buildings.

The Cradle of European Slavery-Era Architecture (Part 1) 313

— Chin

No one can deny that architecture can represent the culture of an era because architecture is truly a good history recorded in stone.

Victor Hugo said: In the world before six thousand years, architecture was merely a great chronicle of humanity. From it, not only are there religious symbols, but also the emergence of human thought, all contained within its pages.

Ancient architecture clearly shows us the habits, daily work, and beliefs, difficulties, and fears of people at that time. Because the people of that time could not write and read as we do now, and even in the Middle Ages, very few people could read books, so they had to record their behavior and thoughts on wood and stone, leaving them behind as materials for us to study ancient culture today.

Therefore, the architecture of a country can reflect the thinking and creativity of that country. The various houses we see are not built without a reason; they all represent the degree of cultural progress within an era. Although many of the construction methods are clumsy and some are ingenious, the ultimate meaning is still worth studying.

(A) Architecture on the Banks of the Nile

Four thousand years before the birth of Christ, the people on the banks of the Nile were already very enlightened. They lived in cities and were able to do many exquisite works of art. Therefore, in Egypt, we discovered the birthplace of architecture. The great pyramids there, the single-bodied sphinx, and the many majestic temples and tombs all represent the essence of this mysterious ancient country, while also telling us about the lives and characteristics of the Egyptian people.

In Egypt, there are a total of seventy-five large pyramids. Their size, solidity, and simplicity represent the thoughts and perseverance of the Egyptian people. The largest one has a base of 7,746 feet on each side, and the bricks used to build it must be at least 3.3 million. Such a huge number may be difficult for you to imagine for a while, so let me give you an analogy. If we dismantle these bricks and build a very solid city wall, its length could encircle the entire country of France!

These majestic pyramids are not religious buildings, like pagodas in our Buddhist culture, they are the tombs of ancient Egyptian kings. Because these kings were afraid that after their death, someone would come and damage their bodies, and that many priceless treasures buried with them would be stolen, they built these huge and solid tombs, thinking they were completely safe and could last for thousands of years. Who knew that their bodies would still be returned to nature, not even a bone would be left to this day, and what remains is the pyramid that has endured for more than five thousand years, retaining the glory of their lives for generations to come.

Next are the magnificent ancient temples in Egypt. They also generally display a simple and solid structure, with many exquisite carvings, but in terms of structure, they rely only on thick, straight stone pillars, slabs, and lintels. The inside of the temples is very dark and bizarre. The worshipers must pass through a courtyard with colonnades, and then to a dimly lit hall, where the statue of the Egyptian god is enshrined in the center. They are also almost as dim and mysterious, surrounded by countless spells, incantations, and strange rituals, and will never see the light of day.

A large temple in Karnak, named Ammon, is the most prominent. Its form is very similar to our current cathedrals, but its completion took hundreds of years. From the paintings on the surrounding walls, we can see a difficult process at that time. The temple was started around 2400 BC, and a courtyard surrounded by many great colonnades was added a few hundred years later. In 1350 BC, the majestic main hall was finally built. This is probably an unprecedentedly large building. The volume of the main hall is extremely large, reaching 340 feet in length and about 170 feet in width. Its roof is supported by 134 thick pillars. Its magnificence and beauty are unprecedented.

But such a great building would certainly not have been successful in another era. Because at this time, the system of slavery was prevalent, and the country drove prisoners to do endless hard labor. We can imagine from the upright stone pillars, the scene of tens of millions of people working under the whip, chiseling huge granite blocks with a small chisel. We also seem to hear the cries of those poor animals as they dragged such a heavy stone pillar through five hundred miles of dry desert. Therefore, although Egyptian architecture, in its simple and solid shape, can be called magnificent, it leaves traces of the slave system, containing infinite fear. This fear was, on the one hand, in the king, who feared the insecurity after his death: and on the other hand, in the laborers who feared that the whip would be applied to their own bodies.

Investigation of New Zealand Commercial Forest Enterprises 314

Translated from the Auckland Star, April 14th

A large-scale new enterprise is emerging within the province of Auckland. Its future success or failure, though subject to unpredictable factors, is fueled by an ambition sufficient to attract the attention of all parties concerned throughout the territory. The planting, preservation, and marketing of its new forests are gradually catching up with sheep farming and dairy farming as the primary sources of wealth in the fertile lands of New Zealand. The evidence for this is found in the softwoods of Taupo, Putaruru, and the surrounding areas. In recent years, several companies have assisted the National Forestry Department in its afforestation efforts. However, the largest and most prominent in this endeavor is the New Zealand Perpetual Forests Limited. Its operational performance serves as a model. The company is developing desolate lands in Taupo, Rotorua, and other places, reportedly capable of supporting the planting of millions of softwood trees. Since 1925, Perpetual Forests Limited has planted 150,000 acres of forest, totaling 122.5 million trees. This land, previously barren, now encompasses no less than 250 square miles of planted areas. These approximate figures, though subject to variation, are based on accurately compiled official statistics. All who visit the forest agree with this assessment.

Factory Chimney Construction Methods 315

— Xi Hao

One of the important industrial buildings

Any power plant needs an appropriate amount of air to be introduced into the boiler to assist combustion. The adjustment of this appropriate amount of air must rely on the chimney. Therefore, the importance of the chimney has been recognized by general engineers. At the same time, its height, materials, and all construction methods have been carefully studied by engineers and considerable achievements have been made. The diameter of the chimney cannot exceed 8% of its height. Its height is sometimes determined by the type of coal or other fuel, as shown in the table below:

Fuel Chimney Height (feet)

Grass or Wood 35

Bituminous Coal Lumps 100

Ordinary Coal Granules 100

Ordinary Bituminous Coal 115

Small Coal Lumps or Anthracite 125

Anthracite Fine Particles 150

There are many materials for building chimneys, such as brick, tile, cement, steel, etc., which are described as follows:

1. Brick Chimneys – Chimneys built with bricks are generally constructed in two parts, namely the outer ring and the inner ring. Firebricks are often embedded to strengthen them. An air space is usually left in the middle of the outer and inner rings, so that the inner ring can freely expand and contract. Brick chimneys are very expensive to build, and their lifespan is forty to fifty years.

2. Tile Chimneys – Tile chimneys are built with hollow tiles. They do not have a firebrick lining, are very light, and are very inexpensive to build, but they are not as strong as brick ones.

3. Cement Chimneys – The strongest and most expensive chimneys are cement chimneys. They are poured entirely of pure cement, without joints. Light weight and space saving are their characteristics. They are most suitable for large-scale factories. If they are built well, their lifespan can be extended indefinitely, but they are not needed for small-scale factories.

4. Steel Chimneys – Factories with ordinary medium-to-low capital all build relatively inexpensive steel chimneys. They are created by dismantling used boiler plates. They are nailed to very strong supports (using extremely large screws).

These supports must be sufficiently strong to avoid any risk of damage. The inside of this type of steel chimney should be lined with firebricks all the way to the top, so it is very heavy. The outside is often painted to prevent the steel from rusting in the air, because the smoke contains a small amount of acid (usually dilute sulfuric acid), which has a very severe corrosive effect on steel. Therefore, the lifespan of a steel chimney is only twenty to thirty years, which is very suitable for small-capital factories.

On Theater Architecture (Part 1) 316

— Ying Dai

The times are constantly advancing. The art of architecture is also keeping pace with the times. So, undoubtedly, the architecture of theaters is also evolving rapidly. Looking at the city of Shanghai alone, the theaters of a dozen years ago and the most recent theaters, in comparison, differ not only in form but also in architecture. Therefore, if we want to build a theater that is suitable for the times, we should pay attention to both the architecture and the equipment. And because of the different environments and different locations, the same theater that is suitable for building in Location A may not be suitable for building in Location B. What follows are just some common issues in building theaters.

(1) Form The question of form is certainly very important when building a theater. Regardless of the size, a theater, in terms of form, must at least not have any vulgar colors in its splendor. In other words, it must meet the conditions of artistic and modern. When the audience walks to the entrance of the theater, they will immediately develop a sense of beauty for the architecture of the theater. Even people who do not want to go in, will be attracted by the allurement and want to go inside to see the internal style.

(2) Stage In addition to showing films every day, a theater must build a stage below the screen for performances, singing, and dancing. Usually, the stage and the screen are completely at the same focal point. But for the setting of the stage, it should not be too large or too small in form. It should be moderate. It should not be too large or too small. It should be moderate. And, more importantly, the open space on the stage can be fully seen by every audience member in the theater.

(3) Seating Seating is also very important in a theater. The first requirement for seating is spaciousness, so that the audience feels very comfortable sitting inside. The configuration of the seats is closely related to the stage. It is essential that the line of sight from each seat can reach the screen or stage directly. Although some theaters must be crescent-shaped, if the construction is proper, the audience sitting on the side can see the screen or stage completely the same as those in the center, and they do not feel that they are sitting on the side.

(4) Paint The color of the paint applied to the outside of the theater should of course be beautifying, with a magnificent and elegant color in greatness. And in the inside of the theater, the control of various colors should be appropriate. Walls. Ceiling. Pillars. Chairs. Stage. If it is all one color, it seems too monotonous. But if there are too many colors and too bright, it feels vulgar. The distribution should be appropriate. On the ceiling and walls, snow white and scarlet have long become the colors of the past. Now, colors that are generally used are blue, yellow, white, etc. in harmony.

(5) Lighting In the past, when we walked into a theater, we often saw many lights, shining like daylight. In fact, this method is completely wrong. After the lights are too strong, it is easy to damage the audience's eyesight. Especially before the movie starts, the room is brightly lit. After it starts, it is completely dark. A sudden change from light to dark most easily damages people's eyesight. Therefore, newly built theaters now often clip the electric lights in the ceiling or walls, or use reflected light so that the light is not too bright, and will not shine directly into the audience's line of sight.

(6) Entrance The road in front of the entrance to a theater should be wide, and entry and exit should be convenient. If the theater is located with roads on two or more sides, then it is best to have two or more entrances. This makes entry and exit and ticket purchases very convenient. When one group finishes and another group starts, the audience of the two groups will not feel crowded when they are entering and exiting at the same time. And with two or more ticket sales points, the audience will avoid crowding when buying tickets.
